En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of an arrow, if it is from a small body, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is from a large body that can be felt, perform an extraction with tweezers; and it is lighter to remove what is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of earwigs from ears, when you have tried to cure them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, it is necessary that you look at the ear with sunlight: if any worms appear, then treat them with fine tweezers; and if none appear, then take a catgut needle of which this is the form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let it be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle tip of the needle into the ear according to the quantity of the pain of the patient, then suck well with the entire thread; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, stop around the thread with cotton as I said in the wound; and if they do not appear more freely as we have said, administer distillations which the ancients have tried in the occasion of earwigs, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or tin, narrow below to one small hole, and above for distillation. And in order to press the contents inside during distillation, have a well-made tin instrument for this purpose, and if you see fit, take a razor and wrap cotton around the point; then pour your oil or juice into it, and all of your medicines that you have put into the thread, and the thread should be in the ear; then insert the contents inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled out or nearly gone from the ear; and let the patient feel what is happening, and it is a distillation of one small pot warmed up over the fire so that you can distill it in the ear; and be careful not to make it too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Il semble que nous avons terminé la lecture de cet extrait ancien qui parle du traitement des vers dans les oreilles. Si vous voulez continuer à traduire ou discuter de ce texte, je suis à votre disposition !
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	C'est vrai ! Le texte mentionne que les enfants naissent avec des orifices dans leurs oreilles (probablement une référence aux fosses du tympan), et cela peut également se produire chez les adultes en raison d'une congestion ou d'une inflammation de la peau ou de l'épithélium dans l'oreille. Et il décrit comment le pus peut s'accumuler dans ce petit espace, créant ainsi un trouble qui peut être difficile à diagnostiquer sans examen minutieux.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Donc, lorsque le trouble dans l'oreille ne peut pas être vu à l'œil nu, il s'agit probablement d'une infection plus grave qui nécessite une intervention médicale. Et si, en revanche, on voit l'apparition d'un pus ou d'une opilation (probablement une référence à un liquide épais et clair), alors il convient de mettre l'oreille du malade au soleil pour voir ce qui se passe.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sure and cut away in front of and behind all flesh, so that it does not damage the ear; if the operation is on cartilage or core of the ear, then hold it with subtle forceps and gently scrape it, until all the cartilage is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the operation is deep in the ear, then take a subtle and light razor, and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the core of the ear. If you feel the operation where the patient feels pain when hearing, scrape lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a plug according to the size of the hole, and smear with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this in no day until the wound is healed, or you take a plug and smear it with rose water, and powder of vitriol boiled; and if you see the ear swelling, then cover that you remove the plug and insert another moistened plug made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it as long as it is sound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is a discharge of pus that comes out, then dip a sponge and wring it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments which remove the discharge of pus that are or treat the distillations.
de la char des papieres	From the skin of papers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the whole process that comes with them on papers when they are moist and dry, so you should stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off a part of its roots; then put it on glass to dry.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if you don't remove the skin, then burn it with a subtle lenticular cautery and the cauterizer afterwards is worth nothing; and they often repair it, but no part remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, the burnt roots remain and do not come back.
de la gresle	Of frost.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Often times they come on papers from them certain things that seem like frost in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of large moist spots on the paper above and below; the operations are such: be careful if the grandine moves from one side to the other, it's a light thing to know; then make it wide, then peel off each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and cut it. If you can't cut it without piercing the paper slightly, don't hurt anything in the patient; and if the tear is large, sew it up with a seam, and cure it until it's healed; and if it's small, do nothing to it, because the ointments will restore and heal the skin so quickly.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn over the paper and take the grandine with tweezers, cut it and press it from one side to the other; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, that's nothing. And when the grandine is cut, remove the scab with a sharp knife and cure the place where the skin will grow back as soon as possible so that the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat or omentum (a fatty membrane in the abdominal cavity) of animals, likely used for medicinal purposes.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fatty substance that is secreted in the form of toads on paper, and this happens more often in children than in anyone else, and it causes a lot of pain to their eyes. They come with catharsis (diarrhea) in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for that reason, they go to bed with their faces always covered, sleep on top of them, and have damp papers underneath their eyelids moistened by the exinach which appears in the eye. And when you press the area around your eyes with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	The method of treatment is as follows: the patient puts their head on your shoulder, and then take a linen cloth and set up a makeshift tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach that exists in each part. Then place it over the affected area; press with both hands from one side to the other so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take a whole piece of cloth soaked in oil and wrap it between your shoulders at the back, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to add to the crack, that you do not reach all the way to the eye, that you injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the iron has not appeared at the beginning of the crack, then push it slightly further into the crack until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then dip cloth in oil and water, and put it on the place, and pull back the flesh.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who burn silk and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains; then care for it until it is healed. And if it comes to a boil with a hot abscess, cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on paper that are added to the natural ones and are inflamed, they cause harm and bring about ways of diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albugine, so much so that it causes the destruction of themselves; and the cure is in four manners: or by cauterizing together fire, or by medicinal water according to what is written before or the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your own hand, then turn the paper soaked in oil onto your left hand; if it has turned over, it's good; if not, put a needle on one thread of the paper and insert it into all the hairs that have grown there. And do this at the edge of the paper where the new hairs have grown next to the existing ones, and pull out one thread from the top of the entire paper, and turn it under the razor; then make an incision in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, all along the length of the tear, from the large tear to the small one. Then take out one thread and put a small patch of cotton and linen underneath the paper, then sign over the paper a shape like a myrtle sprig, and whatever shape you see the paper has taken, it is necessary that the figure be according to it.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if it needs to be cut, then cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper has become softened; then make an incision all along the length of the tear, from the large tear to the small one. And make one of the cuts near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the wound, then scrape out all the pus; then sew up the two lips with a stitch made from a fine wool thread and squeeze out the blood, and dry the excess string on both sides of the wounds, if you see fit to do so. And if not, don't bother, then leave the stitches and threads alone for three or four days, then cure the wound without the stitches with things that are drying and constricting, because the paper will revive at the exact point of the wound and its assembly, but the stitches are weak (as the ancients said), and this is a work without fear.

et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And whenever it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: if it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suturing in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the horns is thus: and it is that you turn the paper and make a slit in it according to what I have said, and then make 2 small canines by art, and 2 thin strings as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and take hold of the .ij. strings from each part where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of what ascends from the paper of oil, and strain the two canines from both parts together; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which has been strained will die and darken and peel, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	It looks like we're in the midst of a medieval medical text!
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil. Then insert the needle into the entire length of the chase on the root of the hair attached, and make it pierce through quickly until you have drawn out the thread from above the natural hair; then draw out the thread up to the end of the skin on the paper with the natural hair.

And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull out the thread from underneath all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes out through the hole above and you can see it by the sight of the eye; then you will pull out the thread and the chase, and close the eye and let the bandage stay closed for two or three days, so that the hair grows in its place and the skin heals; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural ones, and it should be raised with the one that you leave, until it is elongated and then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet !
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or the pustule comes into the eye, there are two ways for it to happen: one natural and the other unnatural. And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or an incision, or a cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to work on it is that you split open that wound and separate its lips, and put in a linen compress and tie it until it heals; and it is not necessary for you to use in its treatment things that dry up and constrict. For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first time; but there are working things that soften, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or althea root cooked down, and ointments made from melted olive oil; and I wrap it in a compress, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care not to let it close up again in the form it was before; and these works we have mentioned are no more than counter-remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	the flesh (or tissue) that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is under the eye and is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from a wound, or cut, or cauterization, or similar things; and the method of working on it is that you take a needle with two threads, and put it in the flesh, and make it pierce through both tear ducts, so that the thread comes out in two holes of the flesh. Then place the flesh above the whole needle, and cover it with a splint one spatulum wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper figure returns to its proper shape according to what is necessary, that's good. If not, take a razor and put it in the incision, and turn the paper over, and make two incisions or cuts on either side of the paper; and let the holes of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision you have made, so that when they are assembled, the figure will be like the figure of a letter called ".j. griesche" (I'm not sure what this means). Then remove the flesh from underneath the paper, according to the amount that its edges are roughened beneath, then reattach the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of linen. Then follow the cure of those things we have mentioned, such as soothing medicines and compresses, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or incision or cauterization, it is fitting that you make a plain incision under the papers, and follow what was said before. Then take a tente (a type of bandage) and separate the two layers of it, as I have said. And the operation should be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters devise machines with all their might to make the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick person themselves, according to what seems fitting in terms of treatment and instruments, in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the sudden movement of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this joining has been done in such a way that the paper on top is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is fitting to insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up. And bind it with bandages so that you sew what is damaged at the delicate thread, which should not be too rough nor too sharp, so that the sick person cannot suffer from the thread being too rough and hurting the eye; and your incision, from which you will remove this assembled part, should be made lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape. And all of this assembled part is healed, and there is no more liquid discharge in the eye, and it is elevated with a sweet liquid, and a colander; then place between the paper and the eye a linen bandage, and put on the eye a moist wool pad soaked in egg white; and after three days use a colander and things that clean out, until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the inflammation of the eye (from "l'ungle" which means "inflammation", "swelling")
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is known that the inflammation of the eye can occur in two ways: it can be nervous and resemble a hard dry scab, or another type that is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and treated with pincers cannot be reduced; and both types of appearance begin near the large tear duct and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye, all the light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of making the incision is that the sick person puts their head in your lap, then you work with pincers to open up the eye. And take the paper and lift it up, then coagulate the inflammation with pincers of small double stitch, and hold it above. Then take a needle and insert one hair from a horse, cow or bull, and a strong thread, and fold back the point of the needle a little bit and insert it into the inflammation, and perforate all the way to the eye of the needle, and tie the inflammation with a thread and hold it above. And then remove all the hairs that are on the edge of the inflammation next to the eyelash, leaving just enough for the natural lash, so that through the incision the accustomed flow of tears does not come. And sometimes bind the inflammation only with string and thread, as we have said; then scrape away all the scabbed tissue from which is this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the thread of the needle does not touch the tender tissue and break it, and that the eyelash is not perforated. And after the incision pour into the eye a little bit of burnt silk thread, and a collier made of litharge, and let it alone until the next day; then treat him with whatever is necessary until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the inflammation is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the stitches cannot get in, this type of inflammation is often cured with medicines; and it grows as I have said in the division, and if you see it spreading, work on the eye of the sick person, and take a thread that is lightly sharpened to a point, according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And wipe the inflammation above with a subtle touch, and if you see that it does not decrease at all and the pus is pressing, distill from your mouth into the eye a collier made of litharge and red collier and burnt silk thread, and stop the eye until the next day; then start again the other treatment according to the same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no obstacle in the eye, such as a boil or an apostema (a type of abscess), then let it heal and first treat the hot apostema until it is healed; then start again with the same treatment, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the eyelash tissue is causing harm to the eye by great damage, then suspend it with a thread and remove a part of it, but not all, so that the flow of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red collier which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the tissue that grows on the eyelid (from "char" meaning "tissue", "growth", and "prunelle" meaning "eyelid")
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Some people's eyelids grow a red tissue that covers the eyelid and stretches over the paper and turns to the outside, and it resembles a rose petal. And the treatment is as follows: the sick person places their head in your lap, then you work with pincers to open up the eyes, and tie up all that red tissue with convenient stitches for this type of thing, and hold it at the force; then remove the first layer of tissue, and go on cutting with a razor until the end, and be careful not to hurt the eye during the treatment. And let the incision of the scab be as we have said in the incision of the inflammation and the small forces by which one removes the scab, as the form shows after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the tissue has been removed, then apply to the eye burnt silk thread or distill red collier which resembles corrosive medicines, and place on top of the eye cotton with egg white, so that it is secured against hot apostema. And if there remains nothing and the wound cools down and you doubt that it was a hot apostema, then leave the eye alone and treat the apostema with soothing things for hot apostema; then return to your treatment until it is healed, and thus make all the tissues that have been attached to the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in any case, it is necessary that you alleviate the treatment of each weak eye, whether by natural means or accidental means with iron treatments; and do not insert your hand into any of these treatments until you see that this member has suffered from that treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the tears of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The tears that are red and covered on the eye, and allow the eye to work its treatment and weaken the eye forever. It is necessary for the first person who sees the eye, in which the tear is, is bad, and there is no other external disease besides the tear; then tie up those tears with a thread in this way: command the sick person to put their head in your lap, then suspend those tears with all a string according to their wisdom, and let the stitches be subtle and double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two threads by degrees in one knot according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then one should apply force to those veins gently, and press the blood hour by hour after another, until you see remove those veins far from the eye; and be sure that you do not harm the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at the hour of midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not miss what is happening in those veins; and when you have done this, then let green and red collyrium distill into the eye to corrupt what remains in the socket.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot squeeze out all of it in that hour, then make a poultice above the eye with soothing things for the pain of those eyes, and leave it on for some days until the pains are alleviated and be sure to apply heat so that an abscess does not form, then resume in this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	They call the hole a "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cauterization and with hot medicine according to what I said before, and it is not healed, then there is trickery in that which you make incisions on top of the abscess, there where it should be dead, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then take it back with all the instruments with which this was done, that is the form; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron into one head sharp, and should be pointed like a lime as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it back on the corroded part of the bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the place with caustic medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is closed, and flesh has grown, and the body of the fistula is closed, and remains like that for 40 days, and it doesn't recur and isn't re- abscessed, and bad accidents don't come from it, then know that it is healed; if not, then there's no other trickery than to bring back the fistula to its original place according to this form: and you uncover the bone for a second time with iron and caustic medicines, and when it is uncovered, take one forest (a type of instrument) according to this shape, and the iron point should be at three angles, and the handle should be thinned down to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone next to the abscess, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the whole forest (instrument) as much as you can until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain through what the blood vessels in his neck are doing if he keeps his hand there; and then restore the place with dry medicines, just as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the wound, the matter will go to the neck; and that is an easier thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	La maladie des fistules de l'oeil...
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes appear to be open wide and there is no disturbance or diminishment, it is necessary that you instruct the patient; then clean them, then apply poultices with iron near the eye to bleed, then put on an eye compress made from a mixture of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla; and then bind the eye up with bandages and cloths. The manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one four times; then place one over the other as much as the eyes need; then strain by placing on top of it a hard bandage firmly, and repeat the poultices to bleed without causing pain; then remove the poultices and leave the eye bound tightly day and night, and if the compresses become moist, you must bind them tightly; then remove the compress after the day and the night, and if you see the eye improving, it is well; if not, then repeat the compresses and cloths and the poultice and the iron until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Translation:
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the veil of the eye gets disrupted, then it swells, and there comes forth a fluid like a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see; then if you cover it, the operation will be such that you prick an awl into the root of the lower part, up to the upper part, then prick another awl where there is one doubled thread from the eyelid; and make it perforate, and leave the first awl in its place; then close the top of the double thread and tie a part of the eye around it, and hold it tight, then extract the awl and put on an oilcloth soaked in egg whites; and leave it until the threads stick with the eye, then treat the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; and whenever the wound is restrained by the stitches each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes are given a good appearance, then pierce it with a very fine awl that comes from the center of the eye, and cut out the moist albugo and lower the eyeball, and insert it right away; then pull it tight until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	The bottom of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This malady called "alcunnati" is not other than an eyelid that is assembled in the eye, resembling a drop descending, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is that you make the patient sit on one seat prepared and straight, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and lift up the eyelid as far as you see the fold come up to your eyes; then press in so that it does not descend and be disheveled the light, and see the things of the patient just as he is used to seeing them; and if it does not come down, know that it is water, and if the coming-down of the fold is not prepared like we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and spread on the thin membrane one drop by the continuation of the conjunctive with the membrane and the cornea, as far as the fold comes out; and when it has come out, make it distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey or hot water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	A more specific part of the text!
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have shown the semblances of the eyes in division, and what is needed to pierce; do it according to health.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, .i. one hour, and if the water rises to the second line, put the fire with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not rise, gently pull out the object by turning your hand back and forth; and then place a handful of linen thread inside, and take off from there the eye that was inside. Then put behind the eye stopped or soaked in oil rose and in abundance of egg white, and bind with good oil.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye by its hardness, because there are such men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", of whose form this is.
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle; then put in almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient an appropriate bed, on which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and you must be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then loosen him in the same dark house, and inspect his eye, and make him see some things, and then put back the tie until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this in the hour of treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you hasten these things, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If there are abscesses that come, then loosen the eye in front of the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, then loosen the bandage and put on his face a protective patch for one day, and he should be kept in that dark house. And then slowly move out of the house step by step, and change to their ways; and know that no disciples should interfere with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Irach (a region in modern-day Iraq), who told us that in his peaceful land he made an incision with almagda, through which the eye's water escaped, but I have never seen anyone do this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of the forms of almagda, because whoever does not know them will see them, and they are made of pure gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these [almagda forms] are of this same subtlety, and their ends in three angled tips.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the navel
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	There are some times when diverse flesh-like growths appear on the navel, and among them there are those that resemble scorpions in shape. If such a growth is present, it may have a twisted or colorful flesh, or a soft bone-colored one. However, if it has a soft and not twisted flesh, then you should sit the patient between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the liquid (onion juice?) onto those growths, and let them dry out. Then take what remains from the growths and hold it in the thin, sharp edge of a spatula on one side, until you know that the growth has been completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be scraped off, then you should open the area with all one of the thin, sharp instruments lightly, until nothing remains. And if it is an abscess that bursts, cut out the scab as soon as possible; and if the abscess is malignant, hasten to cauterize it until the pain is alleviated and all the growths are removed, then pour oil or wine into the navel.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the navel opens and the pus comes out up to the mouth, know that it is healed. And if the pus does not come out as it should, know that there is growth in the bone above, where the instruments cannot reach: then you must put one thread of linen, a little thick, and wet with hands, with about one inch or less space between each node; and place the patient's thread in his navel to their full length, and tie them in an aromatic way so that they come out through the mouth. And many times children at school do this, and it is a simple thing for whoever wants to do it. Then take the head that comes out through the navel with one hand, and the other head that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart while keeping the thread in your hands.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is of silver or of tin, resembling an open lantern, like a dog, and the conductor also; and if you see, make a closed lantern, and have the tools full to purge the head; and have one mandible at the chief to hold it while one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of meat on the bone
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there is a disease at the head of the bone which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large so that it is visible as seen; and because of this it is necessary that you cut it out at the beginning, and have the surgeon remove all of it, then put on the place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays in cutting it out until it is large, beware lest it be hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted tumor, for when you cut into it once, great evil comes to the patient; and if the tumor is of clean touch, not at all of foul color, and you see that you can remove all of it, then empty out the patient and the cut place senseless, and cure the place with dry and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the bone is cut open and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is known that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous joints, it brings little profit, more harm than in some men. It therefore happens often enough, that if you have such an injury, you should look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then sew up the two lips with a suture, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from each other on one side and the other, you must scrape out all the parts of their gum as long as they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and bind them, and powder over powdered dragon's blood and frankincense; and put on the powders a piece of plaster or another soldering plaster, and let it be until it hardens by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is that you assemble the solution with:
des apostemes des levres	boils of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At times boils will erupt inside the lips as a hard abscess resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger in size. Then you must turn the lips and split each one with a small cut, take hold of it with tweezers and scrape on both sides; then apply vinegar to the area after the incision until the pain is eased; and finally let the boil burst easily and cure the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a thickened mass of flesh appears above the gums, which they call "albulus"; if it is necessary that you grasp it with tweezers and cut at its root, and let the bleeding or pus come out; then put vinegar on the area to congeal, or other powders that dry and restrain; and if that mass of flesh returns after the incision, and many times appears, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; these are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are found at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, as rough and ugly scabs; and sometimes the tooth turns black and green and yellow, until the corruption reaches the gum, and it stinks; if it is necessary that you sit the ailing person in your hands, and his mouth should be in your sight, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until there is nothing left; and so do with the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other discolorations, until they are gone; and if one removes what was at the first reason, it's good; if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the scraper that is used to remove teeth from outside has other forms than those used to remove them between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait until it's completely drained before removing it, because if not, there will be no excuse for failing to remove it; since it's a very hard substance that shouldn't be left behind.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	So when the patient is constrained to have it removed, you should be certain of which tooth is bad. Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it's a good tooth, and make them remove the good tooth; but still, the pain does not depart from that place until the bad root comes out, because we already know how to deal with those saints (i.e. the good teeth). And when you are well certain of which tooth is bad, you should scrape around the tooth on all sides, making sure to protect the gum in all places; then move it with your fingers or with tweezers to the first point and point, so that it is well separated, then tighten the tweezers. And have the patient's mouth in your sight between your knees, and hold them tightly so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, remove the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it doesn't come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it into each side, then try to move it as you did before. And if the tooth is split or has holes, it's necessary to fill them with wax, where the perforations are; and when you use tweezers to remove it, be careful not to break it while trying to pull it out. And it's also very important to work carefully around the gum in order to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be careful not to break it, and leave a part of it remaining, and inform the patient through the malice of the root that they will have greater pains than before. Be aware that you do not behave like ignorant physicians who, due to their haste and recklessness, sometimes break the cartilage, and do not bring what we have told; but often cause great illnesses by the roots that remain, or by the cartilage they break, as we have seen so often. And when the tooth is loose, wash the area with vinegar or oil of wormwood and flax; and if there are discharges of blood, which often occur, apply the area with vitriol ointment; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the extractors, by which one first draws out teeth, are with long pointed tips and large handles, which do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles that do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron well crafted, and have teeth to hold the mule.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains to be pulled out, it is necessary that you put wet cotton on the area in a paste, i.e. for a day or two, until the area is softened, then insert the pincers called "algefri", by which the roots seem like a fox's jaws; and they are made inside as well as a file and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you expose the flesh all around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", which is to say "palainche", by which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out through it, that's good; if not, then help with all the instruments, by which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two reins, by which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other bandages which are before in the ratio of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems great pincers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is used if it cannot be broken, and you should know that many instruments of stone are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument on account of the diversity of causes and they should not break the bones or the other limbs unless it is necessary, if he searches for the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and uses gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they are large and well held to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place of medicines suitable for this, and if there is putridity in the bone and it is small, then apply all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural body and the form is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly grown after the tooth and is not in its right place and cannot be polished or filed: then scrape it; and if it is mixed with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the shape, and resembles a small beak, and be made of iron sharp at the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in your hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to file it, take this file with a similar shape to which is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth short and short in your hand lightly, so that it does not move until it is sharp; then smooth it at the end to be perfectly flat, and if the teeth are too pointed and hurt the tongue, it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
