Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb contained a dead child, then she became pregnant with another on top of it, and rejected the death of the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time it came to him some abscesses in the mouth, and swelled so that it opened, and began to great pusulence.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal him, and I thought for long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on him plaster of strong attraction, and came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because his belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I cleaned out the wound, and took out several bones, so that the woman was in better shape.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived for long time thus, and afterwards had a bit of pus come out from it.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have never remembered this chapter otherwise than because, when the master finds a strange thing, he knows how to make remedy.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	This afterwards comes the form of the purse, to which we give the books; and at two turnings on the two sides of the two strings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the pen is more subtle than the stylus, and it is made of ebony or boxwood.
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the pen is one and a half inches wide, and the margin of the trees (the nib) one inch, and one and a half palms long.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two strings are two adjustments of this same pen, which close in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two adjustments are placed in the mouth of the marrow (of the pen) to open when you turn the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, with its resemblance more subtle and lighter, is made of the wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pincers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it has two arms with two adjustments, just like that, one palm long and half an inch wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the marrow opening the whole instrument, so the woman sits on one bed, feet stretched out and legs open.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then insert the two adjustments together in the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the whole instrument, just as you have done with the pincers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the marrow, until the bail (a metal rod) makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and their likenesses multiplied; and when the craftsmen have prepared them, so much more speedy is the work, and higher the houses for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument, then do not fail to prepare it, for it is not excusable in its necessity.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, it is necessary to command the patient to hold her breath, and then have her blow out gently, and the attendant should place their hands over the mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she spits up because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take a pot and make a hole or cover in it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, casia lignea and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in a pot over the fire; then put one end of the string or hole in the pot, and the other head in the mouth of the womb.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it steam until the vapors come into the womb; then have her blow out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine spits up quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if she remains after this treatment and is not cured, then command the woman to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or mullein seed oil and then insert it into the uterus.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and the secondine will be found, and when it is found, take hold of it and stretch it out little by little correctly, so that the woman does not feel pain during the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it is necessary to move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull it out, and it will come out and separate itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the womb is very narrow, we have said the remedy of steaming and the fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she is not helped by all that we have said, then beware that you do not proceed recklessly.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but what is at the mouth of the womb, you must tie to the woman's navel, then fumigate her with ointment of quadruple remedy.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if it passes and comes out again, and she becomes healthy again. But however, when she passes it, a foul smell comes from the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to do fumigations suitable for her: none of the old men have proved that fumigation with watercress and dried figs does not work.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to see like a bandage, and place the head subtle in its natural state, and the joints wide over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and there be fumigation above the coals, and the worm so long as it is wasted, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but rather it is stopped by a subtle syphilis.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it behoves the doctor that she pierce that syphilis at her due time, and not the fundament with an iron spit, and bind the binding so that it does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a linen cloth moistened in wine and oil, then cure with salve as long as it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stop up, so put or pierce a bandage of linen, and let it be left on for a long time, and have it taken out when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And as soon as this stoppage comes suddenly of an ulcer or apostema; it behoves to cover that suddenness: if it is cured, as we have said of the linen bandage.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in the fundament (i.e. anal fistula)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the fundament (i.e. anal fistula) are nodular and grow larger than those that come from near the fundament (i.e. perianal fistula), or in the space between the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if one has a fistula or more than one; and when that nodular one is old, it works, and brings forth more moist and whitish or subtle pus.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas burst; and are known by those that issue or flow out or windiness when the sick person makes an evacuation, and perhaps shoot a worm into it.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if one has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis, and reach as far as the junction of the thigh, and as far as the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows a bursting fistula at the fundament, and not a bursting one.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you beat your finger or fundament, and insert a sharp needle of silver or iron in the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, you insert a thin linen strip or one thread of horsehair into the fistula as far as you feel the strip or the hair with your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and there is no issue of pus, windiness or worm, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not burst through; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is bursting through to the bladder or to the passage of urine, it will shoot out the urine, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	When the fistula is pierced through to the junction of the thigh, the strip or thread comes out at the knee.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the swelling around it goes down, then it is that pus comes out quickly, and neither medicine nor dressing by anointing helps.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these bursting fistulas there is no other cure than surgery, and the vanity of foolish doctors who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those that are not bursting and not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proved.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the sick person lies between your hands on their back; and lifts their legs up to their thighs, and has their thighs inclined towards their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert a strip of silver or linen, if there is twisting, as far as you know the strip comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the sick person feels it around the fundament, it is fitting that you insert your index finger there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if you then feel that the strip has pierced it; and you sense between your finger the flesh or the fat, at that moment know that it is bursting through.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If there's no swelling, then one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is always said that some can be healed well, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help one gives is to cauterize with a small iron instrument according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and insert it all hot into the fistula, until it comes close to the fundament; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that the charred flesh is burnt, which are similar to a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then heal it with moist linen strips and butter, until the charred flesh comes out, and then heal it with an ointment that dissolves scars and stops them from spreading.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, well done. But if not, there's no other way for it to be healed.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the strip enters and does not pierce as far as the finger which is at the fundament, and there is between your finger and the strip a dense covering of flesh or fat, and you see the fistula to that point where the covering of the cure reaches.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cover the beginning of the fistula and insert it immediately before the strip, and then cauterize after, as far as the tip of the strip.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the strip will come out and dry; then remove those charred pieces that resemble a bird's feather, and there will remain nothing.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the skin is too tight and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or a medicinal poultice to make it more pliable.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the cauterization with fire combines two good things: namely, the burning of those charred pieces and the drying out of the moisture and the cleansing of the blood.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then heal it with moist linen strips and butter or honey to soften the area, until the place emits pus and comes out the charred flesh.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then heal the wound with soothing ointments that dissolve hardened scars and are drying medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the fundament and is far from the body, then insert your finger into it and investigate this thing.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the strip and between it are the tissue or fat or flesh, or it is close to piercing, then there is no cure other than hope and faith, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	you must cauterize it if you are going to, or cut it down to the bone, or if you can find it try and treat it as we said first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far in depth so that you cut the ligament which holds the foundation and cause the egress by unwanted means.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps then it will be healed, or you remove that covering and let it dry since it is cut near the foundation, or by trial or other instrument pointed out.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean off the dirty scab which is in the wound as long as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and stop the fistula in the part outside the foundation: if it is more lighter for the sick person.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And at no time are the fistulas according to this manner: and then when you put the probe into the fistula, and it is on the opposite side of the foundation near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	then take a perforated probe at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put 1 twisted thread into 2, and insert the probe as far as the thread is in the fistula all along.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pressed into the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that perforated one, thus as you insert your probe into the foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull out the head of the thread, and join the two heads together, and bind one to the other, and let it stay for 1 day or 2.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and bind it at no time, until the thread cuts through those threads that are between them, and they bleed.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound as long as it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then make it to pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it does not need to be pierced so deeply into the wound, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the pointed spike from which one makes the fistula is very sharp at one end and tapered.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, because those that one must not pierce are not pierced, as you see here.
des emorroydes	the blood vessels
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Blood vessels are in two manners: or they are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they cut through with blood.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are outside have less moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and in addition or a small amount of clear water or a small amount of blood, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those that are inside the foundation, is to command the patient to make themselves clean so as to dry in rooms, until the foundations come out from them, and the thread appears.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and you can grasp it with forceps, or you hold it at your fingernail, then cut through its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the forceps cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them on a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camlet.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your forceps, then cut them, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cauterization.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, then heal with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then purify the patient with a biting and harsh enema to clean what is in the foundation, so that it may come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient feels better, and if the thread is coming out of the foundation, then the treatment is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that you grasp them with your fingernail or forceps, and cut them, then heal them as we have said, until they are healed, and so that the patient no longer fears an incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you make the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into an awl, and then pull the thread upwards and make the awl to pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread around the awl.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too wide; and strain the thread tightly, then knot the thread, and pull out the awl, and do so with all the others, and leave one to tie up any excess bleeding.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave them until they are relieved, and when they have stopped bleeding, then heal them with ointment and other treatments, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying up of the fistula or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there has been a drying up of fistula in the intestine, and due to natural constraint, and when the illness is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you scrape away with the point of a spike or your fingernail the crust above, which does not let it become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it as long as it takes, in order to make it sound again.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then scrape away again with more force than before, until it becomes sound and scabby.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it as long as it takes, until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the fistula (or abscess) in the intestine.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Furuncle is a small false appearance around the body, and goes out deep inside.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds its way to the skin, and feels like a true furuncle, and comes out all over the body, and more often in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread from an ostrich feather, or a strong goose quill, and put that thread on top of the furuncle, until the red circle spreads all around it.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around the entire thread until you cut all around the furuncle, and put it deep inside, and cut out the roots of the furuncle.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, then make it of a thread of silver or iron in this shape, and be subtle under it and drawing on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that it may stay at the tip, and press hard. And if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as it is written in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of an enema.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or vinegar, or melted tin or cloth, and sometimes one makes those small and large instruments, according to which they are made for them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then the ones that are made for use in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small and large enema is as follows: the top is wide, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an outlet or the belly is tied, as you see, and the hole is pierced inside, and it has two holes on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly is made to receive medicines from a cow's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each hole, there is a space of one inch, then insert into these holes a strong thread made from twisted iron or steel wire wrapped around ten or eleven times, and sew the belly together as if it were a goat's belly.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie the instrument in front with a strong thread, then purge, and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the tip of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the servants should press the patient's abdomen together with both hands until it is completely empty, then extract the enema and raise the patient's legs up to the height of their hips.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then press as hard as you can, and if they sleep for a whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge with the enema for the disease of intestinal obstruction, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as long as the patient is not healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the foundation or a growth, then the enema should be just as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of a delicate enema whose skin is tightly stretched.
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; and now we will speak of the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the place or location where they are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by cutting with a stone, and hacking with a sword or knife, or a lance or fist or spear, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the parts of the body, such as wounds that cut on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory comes to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, you must be careful if it was caused by cutting with a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt that it is a hot aposteme (infection), if you make it heal quickly with the application of head oil itself, even if there is pus coming from the wound, and the healing is on the contrary side of the injured area.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and give the patient a drink of wine and feed them large quantities of meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not want to heal, then make the patient's food less rich and do not let them drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put a compress on the wound, if hot aposteme comes, soaked cotton in rose oil or vinegar.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot aposteme, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and not dried by air or powder, which I will tell you about later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound has dried, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips of the wound cannot be joined together by stitches, then join them together with a suture, just as I will say about belly wounds in the chapter on suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is open to the bone and swollen, and it holds together only by a small strip of skin, then cut away the dead tissue. Then treat the wound with medicine, and replace tough meat in place of the skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the patient to eat large quantities of meat, such as roasted testicles and bread, as well as poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or see purulence in the skin that has not reached the bone, then cut out all the purulent part and let it bleed, then treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that is cut and cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie the artery, and if you find it loose, then tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and it is that you put in this powder that closes the wound even when the fire has dried it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making this powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; and three parts of powdered sal ammoniac, and grind it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and fill the wound with this powder, and apply pressure, until it dries well and joins together with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it tightly, and let it be without being undone, if it does not become inflamed; because the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this powder solely of sal ammoniac, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has dried the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has completely dried the wound, even to the bone, then do not put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices made with barley flour cooked in water and honey, until it runs like pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about skull fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the cure alone and not put anything restraining on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but put on medicated oil, such as sal ammoniac dissolved in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber juice also dissolved in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other medicines of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and gaping and full of pus, then pierce them lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then tie it off, bind it up, and cauterize it as necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the windpipe or trachea of the throat is cut, and the airway is obstructed, by which the meat (food) goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	then sew up the trachea above the dog's bone of the throat, and do not touch the throat itself but put it back in its natural position.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it comfortably and let it be for some days, then treat it with salves and ointments as needed until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then cut out the affected area.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, then remove them all if you can, and leave what you cannot take out until the wound suppurates.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it dry up and be bound at the end.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and an abscess (fistula), then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, then observe if there are signs of gangrene spreading to the surrounding flesh of the patient. If you see this, then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on it at first hour, nor bind it tightly so that the blood does not dry in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and the patient recovers to their heart's content, and the patient dies.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put on attractive ointment, and bind it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, then put clean cotton in the wound to suck out any remaining moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four days, or longer.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no convulsion, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor any signs of gangrene.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see these good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with stitches and other treatments until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and closes over, then know that there is an abscess (fistula), and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision of a sword or knife and it is superficial, or on the back, then treat it in the same way as one would for wounds that are not on the back.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder; and if it has made an impression in the bone and has cut into fragments, then remove the wound and take out any loose fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, then let the wound suppurate, it will close the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members, follow the same judgment that we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the large wound which sometimes cuts into the intestines or the nerves of the intestines, by means of which their introduction.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes worse than the small wound that is large.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because of this one puts the intestines back in with pins more easily when they are not put back together piece by piece.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell at once as soon as they feel cold, and thus enter more easily into pins.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to suture the middle wound, because one can sew the intestine back into its place more easily than in two pieces.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is by three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches happen in the belly's suture,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch of other wounds of the body and the two other proper stitches are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and in any case they are more proper with the belly's suture, and I will say each one and declare them separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I will translate the given Old French text into modern English. Here is the translation:
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and another thing to do is this, which is by one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or by the tenderness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are inflamed from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one soft cloth in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or cook it in hot water with mint and hyssop.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and wrap the intestines so tightly until the inflammation is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and once this vinegar has constricted it, and it seems only a little inflamed to be un-inflated.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the inflammation departing, then moisten the intestines with water or broth and let them cook until the herbs are done.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this the entrance to the wound is closed somewhat.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small plug of the wound with the instrument that cuts hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is better than the cut.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	for we should not cut it unless there is great necessity for it to be done.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut into it in the curvature and not straight ahead, and see its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine has burst forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back into its proper place according to its natural form.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are able to do so, for this is worth more.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the navel,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is necessary that you have the patient lie on his back with his feet raised.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and the hips higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two sides,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then arrange yourself so that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to remember what I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, put whatever remedy you have available.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take in your hands, that is to say, the poultice which seizes all the swelling in its hand.
et assemble les levres;	and close the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of stitches.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity and width of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound, that is to say two spans, and he sews a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two holes in the leather with the two points of the awl.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is below the skin inside, as long as you make it penetrate from that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and tie the two ends of the awl together with the four ties;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a doubled thread around the needle by two parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then tie up the two holes of the wound together in the middle.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave another span and he sews another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread so as you have tied the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this until you need more needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	as long as the whole wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be worn out, fine and thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because fine needles pierce all the flesh and too thick ones cannot go in at all.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for that reason they must be worn out;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not good to push the needles too far into the flesh and the leather.
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they pierce and open the wound in front of the stitch;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then prick the holes of the needles, so that they do not bother the sick person at night.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or bandages on the holes of the needles to keep them in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is sewn up;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of sewing with needles is more advisable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it suffices to have one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you tie the two holes in the leather and the two points of the awl together with one needle, having one strong thread between them.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these holes all four together.
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	it runs the needle to the part where you started it, in the manner that one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a span between each stitch, the thickness of a small thumb.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is known to men.
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was wounded by a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than the width of a hand.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it had been torn out very badly, two palms of a hand in length.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I put the intestines back in, which had been out for 24 hours before.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up until 15 days, and he recovered, and was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where you could not find any, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put old cotton over the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching;
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the leather in a straight line, then take the point of the awl or needle that you have pushed into place.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from the inner part to the outer part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the furrier makes furs.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave a space of the awl from one side, and take it up on the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of stitching, which Galien calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is that in which some people assemble the two parts together naturally.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they apply one end of the awl to the other end, in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or point of the awl close by, and make it pierce only that place.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two holes of the awl.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	leaving the two holes of the awl again.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, in two more holes of the awl that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second way of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien says these words, and many people attest to them.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should insert one needle from this side and the other from that side, in the manner of those who sew shoes.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is more difficult to sew than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, and the fire has changed it.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	it replaces the intestines and closes it, then puts on powdered quicklime.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the fire has changed it, he puts on any ointment that is available until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tie up the thread and close the sutures, and sew the awl.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, then put on old cotton immediately, when it starts to heal slowly.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in addition to these, as long as the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound is likely to cause a communal infection of the main limbs,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	you should coat them lightly with temperate hot oil or rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the joints and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if it feels pain or stench in the belly, and many times has happened,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then have them given enemas with black wine, and also if the stench comes to the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and puncture it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jeun" (small intestine) cannot heal when it is injured.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the delicateness and subtlety of its vessels, and the proximity of its nature to that of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts out of the wound, then put it back in place as with the intestines, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, then you should tie the place that is black, so that no blood comes from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are vessels and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the tie.
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put two strings hanging from below the wound to the outer part, so that it eases the extraction when the intestine bursts out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men.
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach.
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became swollen and a fistula formed, and there was also vomiting and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him as best I could, and I did not cease to subtletize (treat with a subtle touch) until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him heal, I doubted that the sickness had harmed his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he stayed in better disposition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced ones said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take two thick strings and then gather the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the string has stretched wide enough to cover the mouth, put it on both lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it closes its mouth over.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then tie the knot and it stays like that, so that he cannot untie it.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another string after it in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This knot stays in the intestine and brings no harm to the sick person.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is tied from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread which is most cleanly cut.
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of that thread a thin twisted linen string.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle and sew up the intestine, and close the suture in the wound.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of stitching with strings is nothing other than through the path of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the gut intestines, there is no cure or healing, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever kind it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes swollen, is universally called "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it bursts out and starts to heal.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is in accordance with the true hard and white nodule, where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it bursts out like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it bursts open wide and at other times is closed up.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and at other times quite large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and has no flesh.
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing other than by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, through lack of blood or nourishment.
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil nature.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the edges that does not allow new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because it has too much discharge.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is foul and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a way of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is slow to digest and slow to heal, and by its nature it flees.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are vessels or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to let you know the treatment of a fistula that is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from great vessels, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the spleen, or the intestine, or the bladder, or to any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the main part of the member and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are hard to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come near the place I have mentioned, and you have faith in its treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you understand it, take a needle of silver or iron, and if the fistula is straight, sew it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, search for a thin thread of catgut.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the catgut folds and curves around the crookedness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot thread it well with needles,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then catheterize through one of the holes.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the catheter makes its way from one hole to another and purifies it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then sew up the wound with your skill, as you know if there are bones or nerves and it is torn deep within.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the sick person carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is near a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vessel,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then tie it up as I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and take out the true cause and the corrupted flesh that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then sew up as long as it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well rooted from its proper place, it is necessary that you tie deep as long as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put moistened threads in medicated oil and insert them up to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply unguents to freshened flesh, as long as it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then let him be cauterized as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then take it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vessel or nerve causes you grief or affects the main limb, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it out until all the corruption is gone.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with unguents to freshened flesh as long as it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and bursts out again, then sew it back up in the same way as before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the bottom of this:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	then uncover and sew up as far down as you can.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and take out all the corruption, then repair the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is healed in this way, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep and you cannot reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other remedy than to let it follow its natural course.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can draw it out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then take it out with an instrument suitable for that purpose.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then remove them all, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it hard for you, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then sew up the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put something antiseptic on the wound to prevent infection.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be like that until the place around the bones is foul and rotten.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will be more easily removable.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, like the one in the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then scrape away only the corruption as far as the blackness is completely removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	and then repair the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted bone that comes up to the level of the surrounding flesh.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it should be scraped out and sewn up all the way to the place where the corruption was, and then treated as long as it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so take this as an example and guide yourself with your own work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so much so that the matter came to the leg and was covered with a large abscess, and there was no way for it to be opened from the outside.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physicians, through their foolishness, had cut so high up that the abscess burst open.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a lot of matter came out and it became a fistula, and there were many holes that all flowed down and outward from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many physicians applied treatment for two years, but none of them were skilled in the art of manual work.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called upon and came to see his leg and the medicine with which he was being treated.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what came out through the holes had a large body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red and had a yellowish-citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a thread into one of these holes, and then threaded all the other holes.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that they were all connected to each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hurried and sewed up one of the holes as far as I could see a part of the bone.
