et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption was coming right up to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I cleaned out what appeared from the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except for the one I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and then I began to repair the wound with suitable medicine over a long period of time, and I could not sew it up.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and discovered the bone just like before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the corruption continued in the bone, and I cleaned it out, and then removed it, and I made an effort to sew up the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I can not do it until I draw around a palm of bone, and the thread runs to all its depth.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine; and it was quickly healed and sewn up.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it did not have to be done again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through bloodletting it often bled frequently, but it was completely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and had no harm nor contrary in any way, neither to go nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be set in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a linen cloth, and place it at the head of the bone that is open.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another linen cloth of a larger piece than the first linen, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head, so that you pull out the corrupted flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the place where you see it healing, so that the dressing does not wound the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a splint or a board under the bone to mold and cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to dress and redress as often as one can see and feel the corruption, and redress again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the flesh entirely; then put a splint under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then dress from one part to the other the corruption, and let the dressing be as long as the length of the corruption is, if it please us;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and dress the bone where it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the joining of the two joints, then there is no remedy but to cut it out;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the tip of the hand or the tip of the foot, then it is very severe that thing.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless you must inquire about this ulceration, how it shows itself;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not make it contrary to you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the dressings and splints for covering these bones are many, according to the seat of the bone and its appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work in its likeness;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work itself will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways and manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument you need, according to what is necessary.
dou feu	The text seems to be ending with a transition from discussing instruments and tools for medical procedures to suddenly jumping to "from fire". It's unclear what this refers to, but it might indicate that some further instructions or warnings are coming up related to the use of fire in a surgical context.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can be ruined either from an internal cause or from an external one;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated that ulceration with the treatment of medicines and it does not help.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member as far as the place where the ulceration comes from;
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the disease escapes by death or by the evil which is greater than it, namely the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems to be burnt by fire;
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness appears, then comes that ulceration from limb to limb.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and it takes hold of the whole body; you must hasten to cut it out.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's due to a bite from some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpians and vipers and similar ones,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the ulceration is on the head of the joint of the two bones, cut it out, and do not give it space to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, cut out at the joint, so that the ulceration does not come as far as the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, cut out at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that is the end (i.e. death).
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy more effective than the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do just the same when the ulceration comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it mounts to the leg, cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to kill the patient with bleeding.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of cutting or dressing the member is that you bind it above and below;
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one minister's hand down with one strap, and another minister's hand up with the other strap.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you should cut apart the flesh that is between the two straps in one broad space, so that the bone is uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or dress it, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the dressing does not touch the healthy area.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and boil come to the patient's body.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if there is bleeding from the cut comes when you work, then apply a cautery to the place immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some binding powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the hurt limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to me in my own person:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	a blackness appeared which seemed like ash of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption came first to the innermost part of his right foot, until it had taken hold of the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long time afterwards the corruption came back in his right hand, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things effectual after purification of the body, and could not cease the corruption;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of counteracting the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted whether if I were to cut off his hand, that he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his country.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to cover his hand, and was healed. (same outcome as before!)
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have recounted this tale only so that others may tell it, if need be.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does an abscess come in the fair skin, and remains for so long that it makes a large gathering of boils;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they rot and burst, and the boil jumps out, and leaves the place clean, just as a cauldron does.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is just as delicate as a silk cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not run all the way to the bone, nor to the nerve, and diseases such as these are called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and they are not even called a "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes right up to the bone deeply, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so delicate that if you cut around it entirely, and just as much when it is fine, like a silk cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal from its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin is healing, and the corruption is not deep;
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with fat, then let it be cut out with a lancet thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	behold if the breast is large, and the boil that comes from it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then let him lance with Egyptian medicine thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take assafoetida and oil and litharge in equal parts, and put the mixture into a cauldron over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes just as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from it according to your need, and mix with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and lance the breast, and stop up the orifice.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and all the foulness is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at no time should he be lanced with ashes' water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	for when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from a vine tree, and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it run off, and lance with it, until you know that the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the sick person cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or the ashes' water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then let him lance with water and honey, or add a small piece of litharge to it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or let him lance with honey and sweet wine, which has the property of cleansing and washing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the sinew heal.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then lance with it what makes fresh flesh appear in him.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take diaphanite plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or lance with some medicines and ointments, the properties of which I have said or the treatment of ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the orifice of the breast is small, and the tube of the lancet cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you enlarge it with a hot iron a little, and put in a tent made of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or Basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, sew it up and leave only one point or opening where the tube of the lancet can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the orifice that discharges pus is on top, then cut it down so low that the tube of the lancet can reach.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the pus is deep, you must not let it leave flesh.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut out the breast so as to see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the pus runs down to the lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the pus is deep, you must not let it leave flesh.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut out the breast so as to see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then arrange it in such a way that the pus runs gently downwards, and do not let any of the pus remain.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast.
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and dress it with a linen cloth that covers the entire breast.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut at the strongest part of the orifice of the breast, one opening a little larger than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then dress with gentle ointment on another cloth according to the size of the orifice.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the orifice of the breast to ease the pus, and do not remove the large cloth outward that one should leave for many days afterwards.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is on the orifice of the breast, take it off often to remove the pus,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes out of the pus, whether it is venom or a large amount or enough, or digestible, or indigestible.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that rises on the orifice of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is healed, and approach the surgeon.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then free him in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change another cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast discharges indigestible pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if the subtle venom comes out slowly after a long time, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the surgeon is approaching. For there are men who take long to recover flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if indigestible pus comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is swollen, add dry medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphanite ointment, for it has a great part of vinegar, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphanite ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and add the rose of old vinegar equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and apply it; and the same thing makes cooked honey thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphanite ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then tie the cloth around, and apply it to the breast, and anointed one does not administer it for a long time afterwards.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily which is also like flour of saffron and celandine;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and apply them in simple or composite form: grind them and make powder, and put it on the honey which I said, and apply it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has gone deep, and has made impression in the bone, or hard members, or sinews.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of this wound is like the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess of the groin.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panniculus is an abscess that arises under the armpit of the arm; Panarice is an abscess that forms in the fold (or pouch) of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps it arises in other parts.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes old and one does not take care of it, then a hardened abscess forms,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and discharge pus as long as the root of the abscess continues to be alive, and perhaps it will continue entirely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there comes a corruption all the way to the bone, so that it causes a foul-smelling pain, and the swelling of the fist is large, and the color is deep red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the section on treatment, and the treatment does not benefit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut out completely the remaining redundancy of the abscess,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is a great aid if the bone and the abscess are healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the fist is pressing on flesh and beginning to putrefy, and becomes gangrenous,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a thread under the abscess that is puttingrid the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up tightly at the top, and cut off the affected flesh subtly and lightly,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dress it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut out the bone and let it heal, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the nail corrupting, then cut it out in a place that is before mentioned.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then dress it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, and it feels a great pain, then it is necessary that you let it heal first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut out the abscess of the spatula blade in a diagonal way above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and take care that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the abscess, for the patient would feel too great a pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of deafness in the hand,
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The fingers are swollen that arise in some men's hands by chance, and they become completely fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps there is such a case where it has bones, and at no time does it have an abscess.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and sometimes they arise in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the fingers' bones.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that arise in any of the joints of the fingers do not numb.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that arise at the joint of the finger, by chance, become numb.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of him who is fleshy is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who arises in the root of the joint is difficult to cure, if you are not skilled enough to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In the one who arises in or at the last joint, it is necessary that you cut first the surrounding flesh up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable thread for such cases, and then dress it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come on the fingers together come from birth, or from a blow, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut off the swelling, if it is so that the finger may be repaired according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two cloths or wet linen wrapped in rose oil, so that they do not become swollen again.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wound is closed, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swellings come to any of his fingers with the palm, then cut off that swelling as it is necessary.
Des vils	The ulcers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Warts are thick, swollen, and filled with foul-smelling fluid that come on many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to them sometimes cleansing with vinegar, and then purify them with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of warts is in two ways: one is to cut them off and let the black blood dry out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you bind the wart with a thread and let it dry completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cut is in this way: first heat the leg with a sharp knife very strongly, until the thick skin is softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg of the patient from the top of the knee down to the part beneath the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the wart in one place, or in two places, or in three, with a wide cut.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then tie it up and let the black blood dry out in your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's virtue can suffer.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it and tell him that he should be fed with nourishing food, black vinegar, in order to recover from the cutting.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the warts are full and cause harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatment of eczema is in this way: scrape the leg of the patient if there are many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and heat the leg with sharp water until it becomes red, and let the eczema swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it over the fire, and then cut into the long place of the eczema on the upper part of the knee, or in the area beneath the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then scrape the skin with a sharp tool, and peel off the eczema from each side, until it is completely gone when you touch it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then tie a thread underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then stretch it with a light touch.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place, above the three fingers; then scrape off the skin on the eczema until it is gone.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then tie it up with the thread, just like you did before, and stretch it with another tool, just like you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if necessary, then tie it up and cut the thread at the heel of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then let it dry and bleed out to the second incision, then stretch from cut to cut until it comes out completely, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot let it bleed and dry, then insert a sharp needle into every strong thread tightly doubled.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and let it bleed, and insert underneath the thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, then one cannot let it bleed or dry out, and it will harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and once you have let it bleed out completely, then put wet wool with vinegar and rose oil on the wound site, and dress it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted, twisted, and swelled together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you split it crookedly, but do not cut it completely; and let it bleed as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the knife with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut completely, so that it only cuts the eczema.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is a curved thickness, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	The civil eczema.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This eczema is caused by dryness in the legs, in hot places where there are no herbs or trees, and on land that has no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it arises in other parts than the legs, and this happens from the corruption that comes beneath the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes from worms and serpents within the body, crawling between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this eczema are that it comes in the leg with a very great inflammation.
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes, and the eczema begins to come out, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the swelling opens up, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two inches, and tie it off.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the cloth stay on the leg, and every time it comes undone, rewrap it around the cloth and tie it off.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it, and wrap up the remaining part, but do not cut into its root until it has come out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and bring about abscess and corruption in that place, and a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	so that it is treated little by little, up to the root, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this eczema is so long when it is treated that it measures five palms or ten.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, whose it had come out ten palms long, and when you cut it, there is a thread or cord that comes out, up to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and the material inside should be emptied, and a medicine to prevent corruption should be applied to the place every day, then dress it like one would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at no time is this vein cut when it appears in the joint of the foot, or the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out with a small opening and then it disappears; treat it then as we said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of a bull", because it has happened many times to oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes all around the body, ascending and descending.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and he feels it well as it moves from member to member, until it breaks through the skin where it goes and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is a kind of purtification of some humors, as come worms and serpents and lice and ascariases from the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts about its wickedness, because when it goes through the body, and rises to the head, and it comes to the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	maybe it gets in, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him cure and pull out, one cannot be sure that he will come out:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it is necessary to tie the place above and below with a strong ligature tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut up [the skin] above and pull out [the worm], and if the worm is deeply in the flesh, and you cannot find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so cauterize with fire on top, until it burns.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that he does is that he corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, then bind under it a thread carefully, then cut up [the skin] above, and pull out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the sick person with purging of body medicine, for the bad humors that are corrupted.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And beware of spoiled meat's putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that occurs in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the upper part of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and shortly after that, I saw it rise as well as a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything, just like sharp silver when it cuts from one thing to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a short while after it ran through the whole body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning around the body, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this illness in that manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often seen many people's pains move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it in the way that I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought to myself that it was because the woman had a thin body and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore the swelling appeared more apparent.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in this way to those who are plethoric and have moist bodies and concealed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see curing this illness, and the sick person feels that pain, if they show it to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then lift up and down hastily, and then press on top so that the swelling subsides to its original place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then have someone who knows how to treat swellings, such as fetid pills and viper pills and similar others, cure it.
Des saiettes	(suddenly switching back to Middle French) Des saiettes! ( Ah, fleas!)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The fleas are diverse, according to their appearances and the places on the body where they bite.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hairy ones, and hooked ones;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with claws, and those that have parts or fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that bites in any member bites in two ways: either it bites first, and then sucks blood from the same place.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, liver, gallbladder, womb, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it bites in any place of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you about afterwards become apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then beware of extracting this flea, for death comes afterwards in various forms.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if you do not see these bad signs, and the flea is not deeply in, then pull it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the flea bites and pierces the bone, and jumps up to the surface of the brain:
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is blindness and madness and convulsions and redness in themselves, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of gall.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it results in swelling of the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is an outbreak from the wound of moist white pus, like a boil, and it also breaks out in the form of carbuncle.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you see these signs, then be cautious and treat it, and pull out the flea if it is not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the liver when the flea bites it are that it is near the left breast and feels like it was stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the liver becomes swollen like an abscess, and bleeds dark blood, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know for certain that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the flea bite that never affects the womb is that pus bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells, and the sick person changes color, and gasps deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the flea bites in the covering of the belly (i.e. the abdominal wall), it is near the small ribs; and there is great anguish and great pain, and gasping; and all the muscles of the shoulders are convulsed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the flea bites in the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat will come out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the flea bites in the belly, and it bursts through the intestines right away, then there is no hope of a cure, nor of extracting the flea.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the flea bites in the bladder, and the urine bursts out and comes forth, and the sick person feels a very painful sensation: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and adjacent parts and spine of the back and feet and calves and similar ones, are safe according to various dispositions. (i.e. the flea bite is usually not fatal in these areas)
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the flea is in the nerve or artery and it is venomous, as I will tell you that happened to me, because you are doing the same thing. (i.e. this text is a personal account by someone who has been bitten by a venomous flea)
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one of my eyes, where a flea bit in the root of the eye:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to pull it out, and pulled it from another side under the fat of the ear, and it was cured without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out a flea that had bitten in the fat under the eyelid, under the paper-like part.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the flea was swollen, and I could only pull out a small point of it towards the root.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the flea was as big as a Turkish archer's bow, and all its body was light without ears; the game was cured, and no bad accident came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out a flea from the throat of a Christian, and the flea was an Arab one with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I held back the beard, and extracted it so finely that I pulled it out, and the Christian was cured.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out a flea from a man, who had been bitten in the belly, and I thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that it had passed thirty days, his condition did not worsen at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut up the flea above and put it in a device, and pulled it out from there, and had no bad accident. (i.e. the flea was dead and posed no further risk)
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose back has been bitten by a flea, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the flea remains inside him, and does not change his natural condition. (i.e. the flea has become a permanent resident in the man's body)
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds harm in any of its natural works. (i.e. the flea is not causing any trouble or damage, it is just living inside the man as a normal resident)
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man, to whom a flea bit in his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out a flea from one of the king's princes, who had been bitten in the eye:
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly declining towards the right side; and the flea was completely swollen.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to attend to it after it had been bitten three days. And I found the wound very narrow. (Note: this text seems to be written in an old-fashioned style, with a focus on the medical treatment and observation of the flea bite)
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it everywhere with great subtlety, and did not find it. (i.e. the flea had disappeared or was no longer present in the wound)
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear: (i.e. the person whose prince's flea bite is being treated now has a new symptom, unrelated to the original flea bite)
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the prick of the flea.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the place a poultice to attract and digest, because the place did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the mark of the flea.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the poultice for seven days, and the wound was again resolved, and the sick person remained in this state for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the flea inside his eye one day later, and he told me so. (i.e. the person whose prince's flea bite is being treated has now found out that the flea was still inside him after all)
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicine of corroding and biting quality for seven days, until it was completely open. (i.e. the treatment was very strong and caused the wound to become open and raw)
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried to pull it out, and felt the head of the flea which was emerging from the place. (i.e. the flea had finally come out of the person's eye)
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed in through the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the flea appeared visibly. (i.e. the treatment was so strong that it caused the wound to open and allowed the head of the flea to be seen)
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and recovered well from the extremities around for four months, (i.e. the person who was treated made a full recovery from the effects of the corrosive medicine and the flea bite).
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then she started to heal the wound that I had put tongs on, and pulled from one side and the other, and could not come out; (i.e. the person who was treated had a new problem, where the wound was healing but something was still stuck inside).
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	so I did not stop trying and inventing ways with instruments, until I took it out one day with well-made tongs; (i.e. the person who was treated finally had the object that was stuck in their wound removed using a pair of custom-made tongs).
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what her shape came at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and restored the wound. (i.e. the person who was treated finally had their wound healed after the object was removed).
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise men judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the sick person was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some fleas: (i.e. this is a conclusion to the story about the flea bites and their treatment).
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on what I am not saying, because books cannot hold everything. (i.e. the author is concluding that there are some things that cannot be written down or conveyed through books)
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters gather well and little by little what is present and lacking. (i.e. the author is saying that even though there may be some things that cannot be written down or conveyed through books, wise teachers and masters can still learn and understand them by gathering knowledge bit by bit)
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	discover new works, and nine instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art. (i.e. the author is saying that even with all their knowledge and experience, there are still new discoveries to be made and unexpected challenges to be overcome in the field of medicine)
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that fleas do not emerge from the members where they are fixed outward except in two ways: (i.e. this is a statement about the behavior of fleas, specifically how and when they come out of their hiding places)
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or from the place where they entered, or from another side: (i.e. the two ways that fleas can emerge from their hiding places are either directly from the wound or pore where they entered, or from a different location on the body).
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out from the place where it entered is a flea entering into flesh, and it jumps out once now and then. (i.e. this refers to fleas that have bitten into human or animal flesh and are now jumping out of the wound or pore where they entered)
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, then it stays there until the flesh is corrupted around it, and the exit becomes open. (i.e. the flea will remain in its hiding place in the flesh until it has caused enough damage to create an opening for itself)
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot come out, then it stays there for some days, and every day it sheds its skin. (i.e. even if a flea is stuck in a bone or cannot escape, it will still shed its skin periodically)
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it breaks through to the outside by means of a very fine tunnel, until the area around is enlarged, and then it comes out. (i.e. this describes how a flea can eventually escape from its hiding place in the bone or flesh by creating a small tunnel or channel that allows it to emerge)
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the flea is fixed in the bone of the head and has gone as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, (i.e. this refers to a situation where a flea has burrowed into the bone of the skull and made its way into the brain)
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have told you occur to the sick person: if it does not come out then, but leaves it for a few days until it is equalized. (i.e. even in extreme cases where a flea has burrowed into the brain or caused significant harm, there may be no immediate symptoms and the situation may stabilize over time)
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the flea comes as far as the spleen, it is death. (i.e. this suggests that if a flea were to burrow into or near the spleen, it could be fatal)
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the flea is fixed no further than in the bone alone, and does not come as far as the spleen, (i.e. this suggests that if a flea has only burrowed into the bone itself, without reaching any vital organs such as the brain or spleen, it may be possible to treat the situation and prevent more serious consequences)
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains the sick person for some days without bad accident, if it is extracted with the instrument of pulling. (i.e. this suggests that if a flea is successfully removed from its hiding place in the bone, the person may recover quickly and experience no further complications)
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very fixed in there and cannot come out further, I administer tar to the area, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it is healed. (i.e. this suggests that even if a flea has burrowed deep into the bone or flesh, treatment with tar may help to loosen its grip and allow for healing)
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the flea is swollen in the wound of the body so that it cannot be seen, then I search for it with all subtlety. (i.e. this suggests that even when a flea is not visible, its presence can still be detected through careful examination and searching)
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument; (i.e. this suggests that once the flea is located and its presence confirmed, it should be removed using an appropriate tool)
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot remove it because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the flea; (i.e. this suggests that sometimes a flea may be so deeply embedded or the wound may be so constricted that removal becomes difficult or impossible)
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein nearby, then I leave it alone until the wound is large. (i.e. this suggests that if the flea is not causing immediate harm and can be left in place without causing significant problems, it may be best to monitor the situation and wait for a larger wound to form)
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the flea if you can, and if it has ears with which it holds on; (i.e. this suggests that when removing a flea from its hiding place, it's essential to grasp the flea firmly by the "ears" or other suitable part of its body)
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you can scrape out the flesh that is stuck in two parts with your fingers; (i.e. this suggests that when removing a flea from a wound, it's often necessary to gently pry apart or scrape out the surrounding tissue and skin that has become adhered to the flea)
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the flea, so that you can pull it out. (i.e. this suggests that once the flea is held firmly by its "ears", you should carefully manipulate them to break the flea's grip and make removal easier)
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and take great care that you do not crush the flea, so that it is pulled out more gently. (i.e. this suggests that when removing a flea from its hiding place, it's essential to be careful and gentle to avoid causing unnecessary harm or crushing the flea)
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it at once, then leave it until the area around is corrupted, and then pull it out, because the extraction will be facilitated. (i.e. this suggests that sometimes, letting the wound or area around the flea become more inflamed or corrupted can make removal easier)
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the corruption of blood makes it contrary, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter. (i.e. this suggests that when dealing with a particularly difficult or problematic flea bite, you may need to refer back to previous advice and treatments discussed in other chapters)
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be careful of the incision of the nerve and vein, and find a way to pull out the flea without danger. (i.e. this suggests that when removing a flea from its hiding place in or near sensitive areas like nerves or veins, you need to exercise great care and caution to avoid causing further harm)
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the sick person back in the form that he was when the flea bit him. (i.e. this suggests that after treating the flea bite and removing the offending parasite, you should try to restore the patient's original condition as closely as possible)
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because that is the greatest help he can be; and if you cannot, then put him back according to what the signs show you. (i.e. this suggests that even if you are unable to restore the patient's original condition perfectly, you should use your best judgment based on the symptoms and signs presented)
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The flea that comes from another place, or it makes no other thing come out of it, or the skin is swollen in the area where you see or feel it apparently: (i.e. this describes the symptoms and characteristics of a flea bite that has occurred from a different location on the body)
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut it then, so that the tongs can take hold of it, and then pull it out: if it jumps out now. (i.e. this suggests that once you have located a flea bite on the skin, you should carefully cut into it with your instrument or tool to expose the flea, allowing for safe removal)
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around carefully, so that it enters the bone and enlarges it, and then pull it out. (i.e. this suggests that if a flea has burrowed into the bone, you should use a gentle but firm motion to coax it out by creating a larger opening in the bone)
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it alone again and then resume the extraction until it comes out. (i.e. this suggests that sometimes, even with careful treatment, a flea may still be difficult to remove from its hiding place; in such cases, you should not force it but rather wait and try again later)
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the handle of the flea is visible, then push it all the way in. (i.e. this suggests that once you have located a flea and are ready to remove it, you should carefully insert your instrument or tool into the wound or hiding place, making sure to grasp the entire handle of the flea)
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the handle breaks and you see fit to administer poultice, then administer one instrument sharp. (i.e. this suggests that in cases where the flea's handle or body is brittle or fragile, you may need to use a more gentle or specialized tool to carefully remove it)
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the flea enters into the hair of the instrument, and then push it out. (i.e. this suggests that once you have carefully manipulated the tool or instrument to guide the flea's handle into its proper position, you should gently but firmly push the flea out)
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the flea is sharp, then insert the instrument with an entering point into it, to facilitate the extraction. (i.e. this suggests that in cases where the flea's body or handle is particularly fragile or brittle, you may need to use a specialized tool with a pointed end to carefully guide the flea out and make removal easier)
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the flea is embedded, it suits that you scrape away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can. (i.e. this suggests that in cases where a flea has burrowed into the skin and left its venom or saliva behind, it may be necessary to carefully scrape out the surrounding tissue to remove any remaining allergens or irritants)
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then cure the wound as is fitting. (i.e. this suggests that once you have removed the flea and addressed any resulting wounds or injuries, you should proceed with standard wound care procedures to promote healing)
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the flea is near the ribs or belly or bladder or side, and it breaks through, and you can scrape over it, then scrape. (i.e. this suggests that in cases where a flea has burrowed into a sensitive area such as the ribcage or internal organs, you should be extremely cautious when attempting to remove it)
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of scraping the vein and nerve, and then pull it out, and then dress the wound if necessary. (i.e. this suggests that when dealing with a flea near sensitive areas such as veins or nerves, you should exercise extreme care to avoid causing further damage or injury)
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and cure it until it is healed. (i.e. this emphasizes the importance of proper wound care and follow-up treatment after removing a flea from its hiding place, especially in cases where sensitive areas were involved).
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to pull out fleas are similar to the beak of a bird, and see this form: (i.e. this suggests that the tool or instrument used to remove fleas is shaped like a bird's beak, possibly indicating its ability to grasp or pierce the flea's body)
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, small, and medium, according to the size of the flea. (i.e. this suggests that the tool or instrument used to remove fleas comes in different sizes to accommodate various types and sizes of fleas)
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the protruding hair is like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to push it to the tip of the arrow, as is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of pincers for pushing and testing if this is so:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the tendons of common muscles
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the tendons by which one heals are ... xxxi, for which it has or the head xvi.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: .ii. tendons which are behind the ears, which are called "tendons of Herbesch" (or simply "Herbeches");
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the .ii. arteries which are in the .ii. apparent temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and .ii. tendons that are in the .ii. corners of the .ii. eyes, which are called "spiracles";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the tendon that is in the forehead and the tendon that is at the head of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two ligaments which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two tendons that are on the upper lips of the mouth, and they are the tendons called "augerich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two tendons that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The tendons by which one heals commonly are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is of the left side, and the common people call it "tendon of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "biceps", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic tendons.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "tendon of the heart"; and the basilic tendon is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "tendon of the belly", and it is above the forearm;
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one by which one heals, which appears clearly above the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the Salvadelle tendon is the tendon that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two heads.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three tendons: one is under the curve of the pocket of the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is called "Sophène" which is at the ankle of the right side; and the tendon that is called "Nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three tendons under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of the tendons that are after the ears helps against ancient catarrhs and migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the healer, as I say to you, is that you raise the head of the sick person.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the jaw or tendons with an abrasive cloth; then twist the sick person's neck like a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two tendons appear behind the ears as two dependent lines from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then you take them to your elbow, and where you feel the pulse under your elbow, it signifies that it is in place.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and push it under the tendon just up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the tendon.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and remove the skin and tendon well for two hands to traverse, and let out as much blood as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then stretch and bind it so that it is sound (i.e. healed).
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I've already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bloodletting from the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth letting bleed of old,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and it is a customary and practiced medicine to have bitter-tasting tears at their eyes.
