et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the bloodletting, if it be so, as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and he feels the pulse under your elbow, and then signs it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift up the key above the vein on top of your index finger, and prick with the lancet.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein high, and cut it, just as you have done in the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the patient, and put your finger on top of the vein for an hour, then put on a compress.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then tie it firmly, and let it be until it is healed; and now I have spoken of their cutting and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting from the vein of the forehead is worth just as much as bloodletting from the cerebral vein in ancient face diseases, and for migraine, and for jaundice.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient twists his neck so far that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point above the vein, and hold steady with your hand, or something else, and let two bloods come out according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then tie the patient's collar, and bind the vein until it is clean and at no time leave a large bruise.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the bruises are too sharp; and the incision crosswise, because the bone is close, and perhaps break the bruise when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cutting of the two veins that are in the two arm pits also helps against them, and against the boil, and against the red spot, and against the greenish thing in the eye, and against the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their cutting is that the patient twists his neck with tying a string around it, just as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then cut, and make the cutting crosswise, a bit of the length of the bruise a bit wide, because there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bruise is subtle, perhaps it will break through; then make sure to close the blood vessel, so long as you need to, and then tie on cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The cutting of the vein of the neck is worth against ague, and against feverishness, and against diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and red spot that comes on the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the cutting is that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his neck to your left hand;
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the long subtle bruise, and put it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils;
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not close well there, and the blood will begin to flow now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood vessel close according to your need, then tie it up for a night, because it is very quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the bruise:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The cutting of the two tendons helps against the constriction of the hiccups, and against the beginning of consumption, and against many diseases, and against epilepsy, and against corroding, and against herpes.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the cutting is that the patient tightens his neck under one and the other [tendon], as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and be sure to place the master (the cut) on top of the patient's head, and the patient sit on one stool.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then cut the long vein somewhat wide, then let out the blood temperately, or as much as needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other part in the other vein, then untie the string, and tighten both veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and let it be until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the cutting of the lips:
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cutting of the veins on top of the lips helps against bleeding in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and splits in the lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the cutting is to make the patient sit in front of you, and tighten his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and know them by that they are black, and by that there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	cut then one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest one from each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the cutting under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The cutting of the veins under the tongue helps after the cutting of the carotid vein, and it's for constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the cutting is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up his tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	cut then one and the other, but do not go too deep, because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck which are commonly cut are cut in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by cutting across the entire thickness of the vein, wide like a myrtle leaf, or in an olive-shaped subtle cut, as surgeons call it, and is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the myrtle leaf is very well-known, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open veins that are full of thick blood visible, and that contain thick and troubled blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive leaf:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicate to cut, and is for cutting subtle veins, where there is subtle and yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The cutting of the Basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps against diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the breast, and the stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is important for the surgeon to cut carefully, and to beware of the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and there is bleeding from it, then he must staunch it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and he should not cut across the vein, but cut in a manner like "anesil", (as described earlier).
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the Basilic vein does not appear clearly, then you should tighten it, and change to another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you can cut a part of it, or you can cut in place of it the vein inside the arm: it appears clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut it at the myrtle-leaf shape "anesil", as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the cutting, then it is necessary that you tighten the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a notch, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the myrtle-leaf shape "anesil".
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to hurt the artery when you see the place swollen, because it is the artery: therefore leave it alone.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it coming out upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, then know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and take your thumb up high, then take away your thumb if the bleeding stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	then tie up the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be careful, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and you are summoned, and there is no medicine present, then cut the artery if it appears, because the head will recede; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a slice of fig bark, and tear it in half, and take one of the halves and tie it well just above the other joint.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding is stopped, that's good; if not, then apply a dressing, as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the bleeding is not grievous in many situations for the small place of the wound, and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The cutting of the vein in the middle helps it to treat bleeding from the head above and the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the Basilic vein and the Cephalic vein, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is important for the surgeon to be careful not to cut too deeply and hit the nerve that lies beneath.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the wound becomes grievous, and by chance cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve appears very often and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you cut it with the instrument of "anesil"; and leave the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there are veins between the two nerves, then tear them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The cutting of the Cephalic vein helps it to treat bleeding from the head, and is helpful for them (the patient).
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to cut in a way that cuts across the olive-shaped or myrtle-leaf shape, because this is the safest of all veins, because there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and do not hurt anything if you fail the first time, and try again.

Des sainies de ventouse	It seems like we're moving on to a new topic!
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made from horns, or copper, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping that does not cut is done in two ways: either with fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the cupping that is done by cutting and blood extraction is done on 14 places of the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	on which one is on the top of the head, and the others are in the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on either side of the neck, and the cupping under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cups on the shoulders, and the cups above the kidneys.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cups in the two arms; and the cups in the two legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not treat blood, but only small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason one has not weakened anyone much, as one does with bleeding of vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not advisable that it be administered, either with fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if through necessity of diseases or by habit it is necessary to cup, let us administer each one an hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and in every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such who, when they have need to cup, have heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such who find repletion and darkness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and shadows on themselves.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and bring up blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such who dream, and see with their eyes closed blood and hurts and wounds and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially since it is in the month of March, we will command them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saliva of the mouth so helps in clearing out the sorrow of the head... that it comes to the eyes, and it is not advisable for this to happen after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this sweating is in place of the saliva of the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not advisable for those who have a cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, for this causes them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not advisable that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold illnesses of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become forgetful, and therefore it is advisable to place the cup more down towards the back of the head in order to avoid forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The sweating on the neck is in place of the saliva of the head and the brain, and because of this it is worth it for the narrowing of the bowels.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for the bursting open of the channel of the womb, and at menstruation, and at fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be put in a bit, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or sickness of the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The sweatings at the two collarbones of the neck are worth for the pains of the head, and eye ache and migraine, and for strangulation, and for the pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of the healing of the brain. And you should command the surgeon to express his hand with care when applying it, so that he does not compress the artery and cause a sudden flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The sweatings on the chin are worth for diseases of the mouth and gum corruption, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the healing of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The sweatings on the shoulders are worth for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The sweatings on the sides are worth as much as the three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these thick veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon to not go too deep, for the place is bare of flesh and close to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and diseases beneath it. And the cup should be large and made of lead, so that it can thoroughly drain. And if it were subtle, it would probably break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs clearly heal (or remove) the blood from the entire body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and gallbladder, and they cleanse the pores. They are in place of the two saphenous veins and the two ankles. And however, after long use, they weaken the body and bring on paleness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the cupping glass is that you first put it empty, and then suck temperately, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the area turn red and swollen, and appear the color of blood; then insert (the needle), and re-place the cupping glasses, and pay attention to the condition of the body, for there are some who have a lot of flesh, and clear pores: it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large and somewhat deep wounds, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we only need to do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we should prick often; and if the blood is thick, we should prick deeply, and the tips (of the needle) should be pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and narrow pores, to anoint the areas of the cupping glasses with oil that is penetrating and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this case, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of melon seed.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in summer, of oil of cress, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person to be cured has soft flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with red water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of melon seed, or water of porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have too much moisture, should rise from ash, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or water of scammony, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or something similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to cure with a cupping glass before a bath or in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after the cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he be washed, when he must be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are cured who are choleric, and whose blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce with ash, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and young melons, and beef of kid, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and middle-aged aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and young melons, and little birds and small partridges.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day that he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give certain people some time threefold or musk before the cupping, or after, in order to comfort the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cupping glasses that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly, navel, and loins, and thigh, because these members do not suffer from being pierced at all.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done to attract blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as when we put them on the shoulders when the blood is not flowing well; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, such as when we put cupping glasses on the belly and navel to reduce the size of the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain when there is congestion or inflammation, and by its attractive virtue, it may happen to remove the congestion, or dry up the inflammation from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and spleen when there is retained cupping, or congestion.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cupping glasses are administered empty in order to suck only, and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in the disease of dropsy, and in such a way that one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs have been cooked that are beneficial for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two palms of width and half a palm in depth, and on the side opposite the middle there is one small puncture, just as for inserting a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be made of iron, so that it is soft when put on the patient's member so that it does not hurt them.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle there should be a rod of iron or steel, perpendicular to the cupping glass, for putting a candle flame.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they are of great and small sizes according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should put this cupping glass on the member in this way:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	ignite the candle with wax or a linen thread, and place it inside the cupping glass across the rod that is in the cupping glass.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the cupping glass, and does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and the heat should be above the puncture that we have mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapor can escape, and take off the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and one should ignite the linen thread again, just like before, and repeat this process often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass administered in the disease of dropsy, there is no rod or puncture at all, and it is not administered with fire unless it is filled with water, and it is placed on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	without fire are administered only in members where cupping glasses cannot be placed because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on naked flesh, such as the head or neck, and other similar places.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find cupping glasses that are in sweet and clear waters without any sediment, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water for as long as they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed with wine and cupping glass, and rub the member until it is red, and place the cupping glasses on them.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are filled and hard, then put them on the place where you can put a cupping glass, because it will be very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then remove the place from ash, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place heals too quickly from the body of the cupping glasses, then wet a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the cups are dried out.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the cup is multiplied, then put on vitriol dissolved, or gall, and similar things, until it is dried out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half-peeled peas on the place, and let them stay until they dry out to the place, and it will now be stopped.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other cupping glasses.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the cupping glasses don't want to take hold, then rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the cup gets out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are dried, then sprinkle on a little aloes and burnt silk powder, or ashes, so that they will now be hard.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the Book of Bruises.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and are a restoration for bruising and purging.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen, dear son, the foolish multitude throws themselves from this chapter, which they never found in any ancient book or letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is the science estranged in our land, for I have never found a good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it, except by the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much and treated in a scientific way, and through experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have clearly described in this chapter that which is contained, and I have abridged it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in the two chapters before this.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we say the prologue of this book, which sums up the words and chapters where the wise person puts their understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when bruise or dislocation or twist or crush comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten and clean the sick person on both sides, unless any bodily weakness such as fever, or swelling, or old age prevents.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the body is very hot or too cold; and apply cold meats, such as cold joints, and bird and kid flesh, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill themselves with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you are sure of a hot aposteme or spreading of matter to the member; then recover the patient with their former good governance.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you feed the patient with foods that make thick nourishment, or they have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and eggs, and peas, and beef, and fish fresh and fat wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with good nourishment the wound heals faster and sooner the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decrepit do not heal well nor mend according to their nature because of the drying of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, rub with a coarse file on the broken bone .i. thick rough ones that harden and join the member together, as long as it strengthens such as it was before; and do not remove its work, and because of this it is necessary to nourish it with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that bruises are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the bruise of the head is different from the bruise of the thigh or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of a bruise.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are bruises that turn into swellings, and others that become incisions, such as the cut of a pen nib for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a bruise with an open wound, and a bruise that has a small crack or fissure all over it.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner of bruise has its own cause and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory recalls to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that a bruise of the bone occurs when the place is twisted and opens well from behind, and sounds on the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or crunching sound, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no bruise.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, fissure, or small bruise.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So it is not necessary to move the joint with your hand, but put on remedies that come later, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the bruises that turn into swellings, and which are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary to put them in line again, even as hot aposthems come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot aposthems come, then leave it alone for a day, until the aposthem is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it back in line with the joint that you can move lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is more gentle than the restorations of those who have fragments; then tighten it, as it should be later on.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and they are from two parts, then it is hands or feet, or if at hand it is small members, or with two strings, or with one string and with your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member back in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are reattached, rub with all instruments the additions to their places at the joint, and take care that through your work there comes no injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if it feels not well to the touch, as if it were not well, then dress it beautifully and do not tighten it too much, nor press it like those who bring hot aposthems and contractions to the member, as we have said many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, then punish the patient so that they do not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither while turning nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, then it is not in place, and it needs to be put back into the condition so that it does not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is put back correctly, so that twisting and turning do not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as fingers and toes and similar ones; it is necessary to envelop them in soft and subtle linen wraps.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs; it is necessary to envelop them in a broad and strong linen, because the wide linens embrace all the large member and tightly bind it from all sides equally, so that there is no slack.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie the ends together with light knots, three or four turns according to the member, and hold your hand a little at one end of the linen, then go above the break and tighten less than the break, so that the break is slightly separated from it.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen a little by little until you take up a great part of the clean area, then take another strip and turn it around again over the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and bind it moderately, neither too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first chapter above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put linen strips or cloths between the bandages so that they are all equal, then tie everything up with a single cord, and then place your well-made tourniquets on top, if there is no swelling or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or hot apostem, then put something soothing and cooling on it, which removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain upon your strings, and be of the middle of a length like a large dog's skin that has been skinned, or of wood from which one makes picks, or of palm tree sapwood, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the string that you put on the fracture is a little bit thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also as long as it needs to cover the member of small size or large size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then strain upon the strings also as you have done at the first wound, then tie on top a cord in length, just like at the first wound over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is on top, the less; and it needs to be in moderation, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the cord is thick, like I have said of the works of fools who make their ligatures with twisted linen threads, and that is a great error, because the ligature cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not need to have less than two fingers' width between each string.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is hurt by the threads of the strings after the straining in their healthy places, then put under them poultices of linen, or torn flannel, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the ligament is broken, I will say the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not need to strain with strings all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For as long as the member is large, it does not need to be strained with strings more than 5 or 7 days later, or longer according to your safety from severe suppuration.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And see here the manner of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour that remains on the walls of the mill, and mix it with a lot of egg yolk, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, in use, and it is the common way of the poultice restoring the fracture to many dispositions, especially for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of poultice restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take 3 parts of asafoetida, gourds, and mugwort, 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, 5 parts; alecithin, 8 parts; and make a powder of them, and mix with a lot of egg yolk. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this poultice, for it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of poultice that is worth for torsions: take mugwort and ground ivy, 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, 8 parts; acacia, 6 parts; Armenian bolic, 10 parts, and grind them well, and mix with water or a lot of egg yolk, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of poultice for joints and separated bones from their place, and it soothes the pain that follows, and is used by the surgeon to cut the bone and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in oil and melted fat, and put it on the wound. This poultice does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot swelling, and properly cuts out the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of poultice that restores broken bones: take dry leaves of a fig tree and earthworm leaves, and grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of poultice for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining swelling. Take roots of ground ivy, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one part; and grind them together, and mix with wine, and if the member is warm, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of poultice, stronger than the first one, when hard swelling comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of ground ivy, and seeds of flax, balaustine, melilotus, and solanum, and flowers of violets and camomile, all in equal parts; and grind them together, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates writes that when restoring a broken member, one should not apply on it something more than wax made of candle wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two states: neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should apply on the broken member things dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is worth for lesions and pain: take mugwort and sheep's wool or bird feathers that have been soaked in vinegar, and ground ivy, all in equal parts, and grind them together, and make a poultice with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then the swelling will be a bit less after that, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place, if so do not remove it for three days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or redness, or swelling, take haste and remove it, and now take off the poultice; and take a light cloth and a moist sea sponge, and dip them in water, and use them to elevate the place, until the itching ceases and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, and then apply dry linen that has been moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it on with a bandage, until you are sure that there is no more hot swelling.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the member rest, and be removed the pain, then repeat the subtle binding and a little poultice, but do not compress it so hard as before; and continue this way until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and inflammation have been completely removed, and you need to apply poultice and binding again, then repeat it, just as you did first in the same way.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if none of the things we have said come to the member, then do not remove it until after 3, 4, 5, or 7 days; and at no time let it be more than 20 days, as long as you see that the fracture is healing and approaching the union with the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then the swelling will be greater than before, and the flesh will grow thicker, as I said earlier. And if you see that the place is drying out more than necessary, know that there can be no suppuration.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then arise the swelling of hot water in it, every time you remove it, and let it be once a day, and loosen a little the binding.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this labor, the suppuration is cut to the member, and it heals quickly, contrary to what foolish sorcerers do, who restore the twisted limb in a bad way: it's malicious, and I see only laziness and wrong work.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Il semble que le texte se termine ici et passe à une nouvelle section intitulée "Des diverses manières de brisure". Je vais essayer de continuer à traduire :
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breakings, and various forms, and the causes are designed;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breakings that are done by striking with a sword, and the elbow breaks all the bone up to the splint that is under the bone, just as an axe or a fist does; and for this reason it is called this manner of breaking "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wound of these two breakings is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is struck with an axe, or split, or fist of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a breaking that pierces, which approaches just to the skin that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if it is a wound that is closed into the bone as subtle as a needle point, and this split is small, and for this reason it is called this breaking "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes the piece of bone go in below, and it leaves a hole like cauldrons do when they are heated and stones go inside them.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often with those who have or had the bones of their skull soft, like an infant's.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and this happens to all these manners of breaking where small parts are separated from each other, just as they are; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breakings by the signs above them, and the inquiry that has been done, and by the corrupt flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary sign is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it lightly with a cloth, if the break opens black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care to avoid accidents that can befall the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, swelling, paralysis, fever, or if the limbs become pale and red, and other similar signs in various conditions, then he cannot heal with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming accident and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you, and it's in winter, then it is proper to remove the bone before the 14th day of the moon that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the skin under the bone may not become corrupted, and the accidents which we have spoken of may come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you make an incision in the broken part so: and it is that you take hold of the head of the wounded person, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the face of the wound as gently as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the bleeding of blood comes to uncover the bone, or a suppurating abscess, then help him with what is needed, and it is that you fill the place with damp flax soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest as long as the suppurating abscess is alleviated, and be assured that the bleeding of blood has stopped; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done in two ways of working: one way is that you cut with a narrow file from the front, and this shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I apply another stricture more larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have a number of diverse strictures, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made of iron; and work on them lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, it should be pierced around it, so that you may apply strictures with awls, not too deep so as not to pierce through the bone of the head, and it should have above the point a border or one circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each one comes back to its place on the edge of the bone, so that you may have awls for all the heads; and this is the form of the three methods of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one awl on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then put the awl elsewhere a little bit later, and do this all around, then cut with the nippers the space of the bone which is between the piercings, and do this as finely and lightly as you can, as we have said, so that you bring out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as pincers, tongs; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone pierced and trimmed, it is necessary to sharpen the remainder of the bone to make a tool resembling a nipping instrument, but it should be sharper and more subtle than the other nipping instrument;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there remains no small bone or splinters, scrape them out lightly with one of the instruments; then dress the wound with tent and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of doing it is that which Galen says, which is simpler and more forceful, and it's his own words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, in the place where the fracture has opened up; so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this incision lens, by which it is shaped:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet up, so that you lightly scoop out the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is below:
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, so scrape it lightly, because you scrape well without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate all the way to the membrane, and the bone is scooped out only on top, and there are small pieces, then you must cover that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have in various quantities, in order to be able to provide what is most suitable for each place, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you pass in front of coarse rasps, and then of finer ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate fractures and fine breaks, you should apply the appropriate force according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily answered by one who has put their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the abscess is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another cloth, doubled in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not irritate the abscess, then apply above it another linen compress, and do not stretch it too tight, but only so much as to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it so for one or two days, until the swelling of the abscess is calmed down, then remove it and apply medicine such as lily roots, flour of vetches, incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and put it on the wound, and apply medicinal remedies without cautery.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and beware that the wound is properly clean, and do not leave any ointment in it, nor let scabs form there, for when scabs assemble above the brain's skin, they will rot and cause great harm to the sick person; for when something caustic is put on an abscess, it becomes inflamed on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any evil accident befalls the sick person, as we have said, then it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if black or yellow pus comes out from it, which is not due to the medicine that was put on it, having such virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them with one cloth, and place it on the abscess.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then continue to treat him in the ways that are necessary for treatment, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Be aware that the two parts of the nose above or the one part alone, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bruised or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you put your little finger or probe into the nose and insert this fracture inside your index finger, and press it backwards, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and be careful that the sick person does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the knee and cannot come to its place, then you should make it equal at the top of a rod about a little big.
