Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do the same again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, then after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling of the tumor has subsided, then bind a cloth made of linen at the top of the knee and try to bandage it with it, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another on the other side, if it is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the knee.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And said no doctor that one must wet the bandages in butter and change each day. It seems to me not well, but it should be wetted with a mixture of marrow of egg and miller's dust; then leave the bandage, until the bone is hardened and the cartilage has become stiffened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one binds on the knee feathers of geese in place of bandages, and if it has a soft cloth around, and holds the break together, and makes the patient breathe through it; then do as you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling of the tumor comes to the knee while you are working on it, then put cerate or cotton soaked in rose oil or in a small amount of diachylon into it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the swelling of the tumor does not come to the knee, then put an external poultice on it, made from sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then place light fumigations over it and do not bind the knee.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the knee is small and it has been broken into small pieces, then take it to those who are skilled with such instruments; then sew the tear, and cure the edges of the wound with things that congeal and bind flesh, and soldering, as with bandages and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the knee, then let it heal with bandages, and put linen compresses on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	It seems we've switched to a new topic.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is out of place, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is just outside, so only, and it is not broken in two, rather bent inward, then one can recognize this easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right part, you should put your left index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then put your right index finger into the right hand, and gently push the break inside, and set it even with the other hand outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is broken into two parts, it is necessary that you provide extension of 2 fingers parts, as long as it becomes even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth are moved or broken, you should stretch one thread of gold, silver, or silk; then put on the fractured jaw grease, and on top 1 double cloth; and on top of the cloth a well-made iron plate, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jawbone, and tie it up with the muscles that you can use, and command the patient to rest, and serve light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure is changing, then untie on the third day, and then reattach what has changed; and put a poultice on it of flour powder with plenty of egg or wheat bran, after having removed the grease; and put a light linen cloth on top, and if the poultice hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it like that until they are healed; for many times it heals in 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess (ou postème) appears, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, reward the bone that is extracted with no part removed; but carefully extract it with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, then sew up the wound, if it is large, and put on one or more suitable poultices to promote healing, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of forceps.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break more than once near the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and detached into two parts, with fragments, and is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is such that when the break is without wound, you have two assistants, so that one holds the handle of the forceps that broke; and the other extends the arm towards the part; then place the break at your elbow, so that the shape be such as it should be, and there be no appearance or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a rounded pole of cloth or linen, and as thick as needed; then straighten and lift the forceps, and grasp the pole with your hand, so that you can put the break back in its proper place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the handle of the forceps to the front because it is too deep, it is necessary that the patient lies somewhat on their side and places a pillow under their shoulder; and the assistants push down on the shoulder until the bone of the forceps is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your elbow, and if you find it is fractured, it is necessary that you split it further; and pull out the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then saw at one of the clippers that you have; but be sure to put this instrument under the forceps to prevent injury.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And shape it like a spoon, and do not make it uneven, and let it be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and one of them broad and the other narrow, just like the incision of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure that the wound is healing well, you should dress the wound, and if the incision is small or you doubt whether it's healing well, you should apply a dressing of cloth and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the wound is becoming infected, you should moisten a cloth with oil of roses and vinegar and place it on the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The application of poultice to the bone, when it is covered in wounds and incisions, is that you put on the powder of the mill and dill from egg whites, and place light compresses over, and insert a spear under the bandage, if necessary;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very broad band, one palm in width, then put a double cloth over the compresses and poultice; then take a fine stick of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the stick above the breakage, and turn the bandage over the healthy shoulder, and under the sick hip; and leave a margin on each part, and when you see that the binding holds the breakage well, and you see clearly that the stick is not moving above the broken bone, so reward it daily, and when the ligaments loosen, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the sick person sit on their back, and when they sleep put a small pillow under their hip to lift the splint up; this will ease the break of the bone by aligning the shoulder, or when you bind the arm to the neck, and do not unbind it except if bad accidents occur, for up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then reapply the poultice if you see that it is necessary, and bind it tightly and leave it so until he is restored; and she is usually restored in 28 days, and sometimes even less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is broken or out of its place, it cannot be seen unless by touch; if it is set according to the figure of the break and reset in its natural form, in all ways that you can, then put powder from the mill with a lot of egg on it, and light stitches, and put a double cloth on top; then put a wide and subtle strip on, a little larger than the shoulder, and under the strip, there are threads in no place of the shoulder, so tie up that thread with linen stitches, so that the strip stays even; and then bind it all together with a strong bandage, so that the strip does not move from its place, and check the bandage every day; and whenever it becomes loose, rebind it, and put the patient on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25, And when this number is completed, then release it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that will get back into place easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone is sticking out and touching the skin, bring it back up and cover it, and do what we said to soothe an abscess. (Note: The text mentions "brisure de la forcele" which translates to "fracture of the humerus", but in this context, it seems to be referring to a bone fragment sticking out of the skin)
de la brisure dou pis	It looks like we've switched back to talking about the shoulder (or perhaps the arm, given the mention of "pis") and its fracture. The text appears to be providing medical advice for treating a broken bone.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; but it breaks often at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, then it shifts downward, and the patient feels great pain, and is short of breath, and soon vomits blood, and the sinews become visible on the broken bone, and he senses that badly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back and puts .i. (one) cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and takes hold of the ribs of the two broken ribs with their hands, and subtly does everything in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is such as it should be; then applies ointments and bandages on top of the delicate steel made from salt or another light material, and wraps it around the broken bone so that it doesn't move; and turns the string back towards the back, and tightens it gently, and rewards every hour with a loosening, and if it has reformed, it tightens again; and if it is necessary to untie, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or swelling, then hasten and loosen it, and remove the bandage, and address what has come up in ways of cures; then removes the bandage, and tightens until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! Vous voulez peut-être discuter de la fracture des côtes ? Dans ce cas, je peux vous fournir quelques informations médicales sur le sujet.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in thick places behind the back, and at the head inside, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one senses this well with an examination of the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the treatment is that you put an oil on the break, if it needs to be done so. And then apply a poultice, and tie with an iron band, if you need to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is turning inward, the patient feels very great pain and stitching, as well as a sort of pleurisy, because the bone punctures the membrane; and they become inflamed with pustules, and become hot and vomit a great quantity of blood, and this is a grave sickness, and the ancient ones have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the break outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot swellings come and become inflamed, if they have not already arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has arrived, then let the healing occur.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And one of us said that you place cupping glasses on the spot, in order to draw out the matter, and it seems like a good reason; however, there is doubt whether the cupping glass might attract the superfluities to the spot because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And one of us said that the spot should be covered with a damp linen cloth in hot oil, and then tie tents between the ribs to put equal pressure on the whole place, and then it should be treated as for a case of pleurisy, of meat ( possibly referring to poultice or compress) and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain because of the bone that pierces the membrane, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut on top of the place where the broken rib lies, and put an instrument underneath to protect the spleen; and then one should saw through the bone, and draw it out gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat with poultices until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck (or possibly "shoulder")
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there comes a breakage in the neck bones and it happens that it bends; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be saved or not, take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel it. Know that they are mortal in many dispositions, and if they can move them and feel well when you restrain and prick them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be saved or not, take heed if the feet are softened, and the accidents that happen in the hands, and on top of the back there is windiness and vomiting without intention; and when it is placed on their stomach, if there is windiness and vomiting without intention. And when it is laid on its back and they want to sit up, they cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not tire yourself in treating them.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come upon him, then the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply salve if there is a warm abscess, put oil of rose or egg yolk on the spine until it is soothed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, tie it with a strip, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it is necessary to put a splint on the affected area; and take out the bone, then sew together the two edges of the wound, if they are large, with a suture, then treat with ointment anointing flesh, until he is healed; and if the ligament of the bone is broken, which is called the "ligament of the knee", put your left fist into it, and place it equally to the other hand in your power, then put on the plaster and the bandage if you need them; then tighten it, and if there is a dislocated bone, do so, take it out, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	The break of the hip bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the hip bone is broken, it is a great misfortune that can lead to some diminishment of the head; and the patient falls on their side, declines towards the backside, and comes to the injured part with much pain, and stings, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you stretch your hand over it, as high as you are above the break; and know what the break is and its shape; and if the break is only in the head, place the broken part equally with it, until it is in its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inside, make the patient lie on their belly, as long as you see a sign of healing in that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it equally, put on a plaster, then put on a wooden or horn splint, and bind the break so that it does not move; and fill the space under the ribs with a poultice, until the swelling is equalized.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms, do not touch it, until the abscess is calmed down, and apply what we have said before to it; and then return to the treatment, and bind it as it needs to be bound, if there are no bad accidents; and that's how you should do it.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The break of the shoulder blade.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder blade is that which is between the scapula and the head of the arm; and if it is broken, it must be restored in one of two ways: one of which is to take a wooden splint, thicker than my thumb, and shape it like this:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two ends of the splint with two strips of cloth, and bend it upwards, and make the patient sit on a chair; then place the broken arm on the splint, as long as it reaches to the elbow, and have someone hold a heavy object or support it from below; then bring the ends of the splintered bone together, so that the break returns to its proper shape.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to have the patient lie on their back, and bind their hand to their neck; then command two assistants to take one end of the splint and place it in the patient's hands, and the other assistant to take the other end and place it under the entire length of the splint, and have each person hold their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the traction is too strong, bind one end of the splint under the break and on top of it, and have each assistant hold their part. And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, it is fitting to put one end of the bandage in the middle of the elbow, and the other towards the scapula, under the break; and similarly if the break is towards the scapula, it is fitting to put one end of the bandage lightly, without labor, as long as the break is equal on top and on the scapula; then bring the ends of the broken bone together, bind them, and keep an eye out for abscesses.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms, do not strain it for 7 days, and apply a moist linen cloth soaked in rose oil to it, until the abscess is calmed down; then bind it. And the way to bind it is that you put a poultice on the break, then bring the arm onto the shoulder blade, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put a bandage on, and strain it on the shoulder blade, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, as long as nothing obstructs it, or if the bone is not dislocated.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not in its proper position, use splints, and put a larger and stronger splint on the break than the others, with a space of two inches between each one, so that each splint is as long as it passes three inches from the break on both sides; then strain on the splints, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, but more strongly and less spaced out.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see that the splints and the straining are in place, as we have said, then restore the broken member, and if you doubt about the abscess, let it be left tied until the seventh day, just as we have said; then check each three days the bandage, to see if there is no inflammation or swelling at the site, or if the numbness cannot come to the member because it is too tightly bound. If so, do what we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, do not untie the bandage until after three days or more, and have the patient lie on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and put a pillow made of wool under the shoulder blade, and check every hour of the day or night to see if the shape of the broken member is changing or if the bandages are becoming loose. If so, do what we have said about using medicine to fix it, and give them food as we previously mentioned, in such a way that the food reaches the first subtleties; and when they begin to recover, let them eat plenty.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "fasciculi", one small and one large, with the small one being attached to the armpit and the large one being under it towards the elbow; perhaps the larger bone alone breaks, or the smaller one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones are broken, the healing is easy and quick; and when the large bone is broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when both are broken together. If it's only the small bone that is broken, then you have to stretch the arm slightly, and put it back in place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large bone that is broken, then you have to pull it more strongly; and stretch the arm up on one cushion, and support the armpit with a pillow higher than usual, and bring the small bones lower than usual, and have the patient cross their arms over themselves, and a pillow in front of them higher than they do, so that the patient doesn't suffer any pain; then extend another assistant's arm to the side of the patient's hand, or to one bandage, and another assistant to the other above. And then put the mirror back in place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has splintered into pieces, then put each piece back in its place, and if there's no gap that can be closed with a bandage, and you can't restore it to its original state, then make an incision and expose the bone, as we said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the separate chapter on wounds; then take care of the wound.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the course of the restoration a boil appears, then apply a bandage made from a mixture of rosary oil and white wax, not too hard or too soft; and tie one end of the bandage above with subtlety until the boil is calmed. Then remove the wax, and place the poultice made from the flour powder with plenty of egg on it; then dress the wound, and let the splint be more sturdy, and a little larger than the others; and know that there should be 7 or more straps in various arrangements: whether the break is in one bone or two; and strain the break more up than elsewhere, and always less apart, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages above the break be soft and moist, not hard or sharp; and let the strings that bind it be made of linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said. And reward the member and the limb after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, it is necessary that you anoint the member with hot water until the itching has been calmed; and let the member rest neither too tightly nor too loosely. And then reapply the straining, and if the bandages are worn out and the bone is separated, and things seem like this, then address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the swelling cannot come to the member, because it is too narrow, then you must soften it with a poultice, and let it be for some days, until the swelling comes, and then bind.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have said comes to the patient, do not loosen it until twenty days or thereabout, then he can lie on his back with hands at his neck, and be sure his necks are equal, and beware of movement and jolting, and sleep on their backs; and know that this breaking is restored in thirty days or thereabouts, and possibly in twenty days, according to the temperaments and compositions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking (or dislocation) of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand there are four bones and eight articulations, and it is broken many times with a blow to the poultice.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the wrist of the hand is broken or bent, then it is necessary for the patient to keep his hands crossed and sit straight in front of him equally; then put his hand on the stretched cloth, and extend the fractured bones with splints and set them even with a mirror, until they are well joined; and apply the poultice and bandages, if swelling comes, then put an iron stake according to the quantity of the lead; and be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the belly of the wrist, make a sphere of cloth and command the patient to press it against their broken wrist; and then bind with a long linen cloth, and let the iron splint be as wide as the hand's palm, and bind it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside (of the wrist), it is necessary to put an iron splint above and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the linen between the bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in any of the bones (of the wrist), and it is the pisiform (small bone), then put them equal, as it should be; and bind with the palm, and if you see that you need to put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and not to move; and if the fracture is in one of the other bones, such as the index finger or one of the others, then put them equal, and tie with the healthy bone that follows; or tie all together in one bandage, whatever seems best, or put a splint on top, as I mentioned before.
de la cuixe brisie	It seems we've moved on to a new topic! The text appears to be discussing various medical treatments for broken body parts, specifically the hand and wrist.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the scrotum are many times broken, and one can clearly see when they turn before and behind; and the restoration is that on ties one thread above the breakage, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each of his limbs to its equal part; and that is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the breakage is near to the root of the scrotum, then tie one of the threads towards the groin, and the other threads below the breakage. And also if it is near the knee, and then tie the thread near the knee, and extend downwards; then place the splint along its natural figure, and then put the plaster, and tie it, if there are any swellings that come from it.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is hot swelling, then let it calm down and come back to your work and care; the dressing is made in this same way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap above the breakage, one strong cloth doubled in two or three layers, and leave the superfluous parts; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and insert a long thread between the scrotum and the thigh, near the knee below, and let the end of the thread come up; then wrap the cloth over the leg and the scrotum, then put stars on the breakage, and put a star on the bone of the leg; then fill in the gap between the leg and the scrotum with soft fabric to put equal pressure; then begin to tie firmly three turns or four on the breakage; and as you go up from the breakage, and less tension; then take both ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the scrotum, and tie three stars above them; then go back down to the end of the thread, as far as near the foot; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone; then it will not come any swelling or appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens again, then remove the dressing and address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, then it is necessary to sew them up, if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the area open and draw out the fragments; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no matter how many times the scrotum is broken in this way, as one puts stars on it, like on the armpit and arm; nevertheless, in this restoration made, the disease does not recur.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the scrotum is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, depending on the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the armpit groove
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the armpit groove there is sometimes a slight break, but it folds many times. And if it breaks, then it's only a fissure or an opening (pertus), and it has no pain, and it feels alright.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put it back together again with what was broken to its place, as long as you can move it; then apply the splint, and if necessary, put an iron ring on it, and tighten it as needed, and then return all the things we have said in other breaks, which are hot and similar; then put something on each accident that is suitable for it, until it is sound.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called the tibia or "mustelz", and the other is called the fibula; and it has almost all the same breaks as it comes to the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm also, and the work is entirely so.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg will turn from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the lower bone (tibia) is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the upper bone (femur) is broken, it causes great pain and it can be seen clearly, and it turns downward. Then apply an extension, and put it back together again, and tie the splints in the same way; but always, it's necessary that if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter, and make it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that surround the leg from one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap them in two layers with a bandage on top and bottom, and tie it in the middle as well. And at this point, the leg should not be able to bend to the right or left, and that's good. And some people give an extra wooden support that is as long as the leg, made of wood, and put it there to stabilize the movement, and properly treat the wound where the break occurred; and every day move the leg to see if there is a hot abscess or another accident, and cure it until it is sound.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not break, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and are split in two, and there is no other fracture except for a crush in several positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot are broken and you see these bones overlapping one another, put the sick foot on the ground, as if it were going to walk, then put your other foot on top of it, at the point where the bones are elevated, and press down so hard that they return to their place; then apply a splint and bandage over it, and place under the foot of the injured person a small wooden board with two wedges, then bind it firmly to the foot, as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days will have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find that the bones are aligned again, whether they were broken or disjointed.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some of the toes broken, restore them, as we have said about the fingers of the hand. Then put a splint on the broken toe, which is one size larger than the toe itself, and place under the foot that wooden board I mentioned, and bind it firmly in place; and if there are two or three, or more, broken toes, then put a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the wooden board under the foot tightly; and make sure that the ends of the splints protrude from under the wooden board, so that they are well secured.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember not to forget the other things I said about other fractures, that we mentioned; and treat each accident accordingly.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone of the shoulder blade (scapula)
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the scapula is broken, have the woman sit up and stretch out, then lean her back towards the part of the back where it broke, and hold it in place by the back. Then fill the space with cotton, as big as a fist, and let her lie down; and when she wants to urinate, take out the cotton, and once she has finished, put it back in place, and do this for about 7 days or so: the break will be healed. And if you see, take a bladder of cowhide and tie a stick to the opening, and blow into the stick forcefully until the air escapes from the bladder; then the space will expand and return to its natural shape. Then fill it with cotton and let it stay that way for some time, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the shoulder blade of a man or woman is broken, have it restored in the same way that we said to repair the hip bone; and these near fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use into them, and understands my book. For the break signifies the right way of restoration in several dispositions: listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and put it in there; then wrap it with linen cloth, and let it be for three days or so: it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound (compound fracture)
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the thigh or arm or similar, to be cured now, so that the remedies we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healing, but then becomes inflamed with gangrene, then you must bind it with vitriol (a caustic substance), and if you have nothing else, start again to restore the break in the same hour or day, so that pus does not form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus forms, let the wound rest alone for just 9 days, until the pus has subsided, and don't touch it again on the 10th day or quarter, because you would cause a bad accident to happen.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the surface of the skin, it is necessary that you make a small incision with your hands, making a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not prepared to put even with your hands, then take this instrument which is of iron, which has 7 or 8 fingers (or handles) in length, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the surgeon to wear gloves, taking 3 or 4, as needed for each cure of breakage; and they should be long and a bit thick, so that they do not bend when compressed on the member at your work, and have a hook in front and are thicker in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a "palainche", for which reason it is necessary that the curved hooks be placed on top of the visible bone; and insert them once, so that they protrude, and are even with each other. And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut off the top of the bone, until the instrument has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, then use a suitable instrument such as a saw or chisel to your power; then scrape out what remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. So do what you must so that it is in its place, then soak one cloth in black vinegar, and properly bind it on; and do not put cerate or other oil on the wound lest it cause corruption and infection; then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and sew the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the breakage; and many times people have done this foolishly and brought death or corruption upon the patient sometimes; and the constriction is softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is foul or large and you doubt that bad consequences will come from it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then do not put on ointments; but wrap around tightly, instead of ointments, hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one day or two that the bow is beginning to appear at the wound, then remove what you have put on it all together, and apply salving for healing wounds, such as tetra-pharmaceutical ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the bandage twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until the member is solidified and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be wrapped in such a way that the bow (or swelling) runs down towards the leg gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if in many days it does not heal and instead swells again, know that there are small fragments of bone, which is why you should take the stitches out of the wound with a thread, and remove all these loose bones that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if an abscess or other form of corruption comes to the place, it is necessary that you treat it according to what he says in this chapter beforehand. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bones of the shin or thigh, and others similar to the large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times death ensues from it, but leave it until it rots; perchance it will come out after twenty or thirty days. Then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	des bosses qui viennent sur la soudure (from swellings that come on the swelling)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see swellings come after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore be careful if the swelling is fresh: if you apply medicinal applications that constrict, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, aloe vera, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with wine for constricting or with egg white or with oil; and put it on the boil in bandages, and bind it tightly, and do not untie it even by hand for a day; and then let it out, and repeat another one, as long as the nodules are removed; or you bind it above a piece of linen well made; for the properties of linen is that it removes all the swellings on the members; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cover it with cloth, and make the superfluousness apparent; or you wrap it in a clean cloth, until it is removed, and treat it so that it becomes well.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is restored and after healing remains weak and fragile in the member, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to excessive inflammation; or due to too great movements, not in its proper time; or because it has too little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you feed the sick person and make their body tender, as long as there is plenty of blood in them; and have them take baths, and give them joy and comfort; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts a great nourishment, and draws out the inflammation with an absorbent cloth, as long as the nourishment comes to the member, and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the deformed member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, even so it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish people who say that you should break the limb all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and comes to great harm, and perhaps death. However, if the nodules and twisting are fresh, it is necessary that they be drawn out with hot water or cooked soothing herbs, such as leaves of valerian, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a soft plaster, such as well-made dyacquilon, and take the pulp of valerian, and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take fatty figs, and grind them with collyrium powder, and similar medicines that soften the joint.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at any time, the nodules are removed by continuous and long-term rubbing with wet hands. And it should be moved every hour to loosen up the member.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and turned to stone, so that it needs to be removed with an iron instrument, then you should cover just up to the bone with a small, sharp incision, and put a poultice and a salve in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	It begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, why it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to anyone, if you must now bring it back to its original place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if you wait, the swelling increases, and by chance if it is reset with pain at the joint; therefore, do not move it until it is no longer swollen: many times this brings on spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when this occurs, make the patient recover, then leave him, until the swelling is alleviated; then warm the limb with hot water and oil, then rinse it lightly, and treat each member as the treatment will come back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	What happens when the jawbones are dislocated and they are dislocated in two ways: or they are slightly out of place and a bit softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to place by itself in a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and fully done, you must rinse it immediately, and not wait.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in such a way that the attendant makes a poultice for the patient's head, and puts the mirror-shaped poultice on one side of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other hand is outside to put it back together; and commands the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant puts it back together evenly, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaw returns is difficult, namely if it are the two jaws together, then heat them with hot water and oil, until they are rinsed lightly; and do not wait for the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly and the patient's mouth closes well without much difficulty, then put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil and wax, then tie them lightly with linen threads.
