et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back and his legs are between two pillows, so that he doesn't move them to the right or left, nor does he try to chew, but rather takes light food until the pains are removed and the jaws are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then gradually eat what he wants lightly, and does not worry about opening his mouth to eat and drink, as long as the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be returned to place within an hour and are not converted back to their normal state, it will lead to fever and bad habits, and possibly diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of cold, clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these symptoms, then know that it is a bad sign, and understand that the person who experiences them will die in 8 days.
de la forcelle	This appears to be a title or heading, possibly indicating the start of a new section in the text.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation (li forcele) cannot be reduced from the side towards the spine within its usual course, and is never reduced to the outside, and one can easily feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the treatment is that the patient lies down on his back, and stretches out his arms; then presses the dislocated place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then put on a poultice and bandage it, and tighten it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the foot that is on the side of the hip cannot be reduced; if it can not be reduced, and if it is ever reduced, then rinse it back to its place, as we have said; then put on a poultice and bandage, and tighten it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly is reduced the foot of the hip, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	This appears to be a title or heading, indicating the start of a new section in the text about shoulder dislocations.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: first, it dislocates at the part of the collarbone below (assele); second, it dislocates at the part of the spine; and by chance, it may also dislocate above, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it is not dislocated back for the shoulder, nor is it dislocated inwards for the nerves; and more often than not, it dislocates downwards towards the collarbone, especially in those who are thin, because their bones are more fragile; to those who have enough fat, it slips slowly, and comes back slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they have a blow or fracture, and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So it is necessary to examine it thoroughly, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation when it goes down towards the collarbone, and you will find a clear difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will see the manifestation of their diversity.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and under the collarbone, at the head of the shoulder, just like an empty space, such as when there is no bone; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their chest, nor move it with any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly at the touch of the shoulder.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is not easily reducible when it is new or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up, then places his palms under the collarbone, and lifts the joint with force upwards to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it down; and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it doesn't come back as we said within three days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the minister should apply a soothing and calming ointment, such as a decoction of wormwood, fenugreek, and melilotus in water, and bring it near.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then have the patient lie on their back, and place a soft woolen pad under the collarbone, not too soft or too hard, then have the minister take hold of the patient's wrist with one hand, and lift the head of the shoulder strongly, and pull the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another minister holds the patient's head in place, so that it does not move down; and the shoulder will come back immediately, and if you see that it reduces according to this method.
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and that you have a person who is larger than the patient present, and he stands to the side of the patient, and pushes his shoulder under the collarbone of the patient, and lifts up the collarbone so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another minister pulls the patient's hand downwards towards their belly. And if the patient is too thin, they can be weighed down with something heavy, and the dislocation will come back immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it can also be reduced in another way: and that is to stick a long wooden dowel into the ground, of such length as a pistol, and neither too large nor too thick,
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then it is placed under the patient, with a cloth draped over it so that it is soft on top, and the patient is standing near the length of the dowel. Then the patient's hand is stretched out to the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it doesn't want to come back despite all the things we have said, then do this cure: take a stick that is two arms long and three thumbs wide, with the top rounded so that it can easily enter deeply under the collarbone, in this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a cloth over the top of the stick so that it won't hurt the patient, and place it under the collarbone of the patient; then stretch your arm across the length of the stick, and tie the other end to the stick at the elbow, and also tie the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on a wooden beam about as wide as a large plow, and have the hands hanging down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will come back immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, however it may be done, it is necessary that you put under the collarbone a spear of wool, then apply an ointment made from mill powder with incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around it; then tighten the bandage under the collarbone gently, and turn the string on the ointment, and wrap the hand around the neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they be moved carefully little by little, as soon as the limbs are comfortable, because they will heal more quickly; and then move them again after five or seven days, and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is still out of place because it has moved or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply cauters to three punctures, as they are placed in front of a cauterizer.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is near the chest, and the shoulders, or backside, is caused by sudden impulse, and stretching of hands, and it administers another injury; and cure them until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness to the member, and delayed motion, then the patient should bathe many times, until that stiffness is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the hip
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the hip is dislocated to points, and returns to points; and it is dislocated from all parts, and even in front and back, and the dislocation is not regained, for one sees it well and feels it well; and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the sick hip with the healthy one, if it cannot be seen clearly. For the joint is crooked, and cannot flex the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it's necessary that you rub it gently while the swelling comes down, for if the swelling came down, it would be painful to move it back; and perhaps it cannot be moved back entirely, especially when it is in the back; it's worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and perhaps death may come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is this, when it can be moved back like that, you extend his hand with yours; and his arm is stretched out, and his hands on the hip around, over, and under, and push the joint to its sockets together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his other hand, and pushes the joint back with the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it doesn't want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and that two people extend the arm, and hold it tight with both hands, so that it doesn't move at all. Then turn the arm from one side to the other, then wrap a double-folded cloth long and wide around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the patient has joined the joint to their hand, they should rub it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint together firmly, until it comes back.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it's back in place, they should put on dry poultice with some egg yolk, and strain it firmly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, and let it be for a while, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, they should remove the bandage and leave it so. And if you see that the joint doesn't hold well, repeat the poultice and the bandage, and let it be for a while, until it's firmly put back, then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels sore after the return of the joint, and it's swollen, then bathe and scrub it gently, and press on it until it's eased. Or put a fatty sheep's fat poultice on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then take it off and put it in the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it's sweating, then gently scrub the joint again, then put the poultice back on, and then put it in the bath. And do this two or three times until it's healed. And if you see that it still hasn't returned to its normal state, put moistened flaxseed warmed with butter on top of it, and strain it; it will return to its proper condition.
li dislocation de la main	The text appears to be a medieval medical text describing the treatment for a shoulder joint dislocation.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The articulation of the hand is dislocated, and the return is slight, more than other articulations Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place hastily, in the same manner as it was dislocated, so that there may be swelling or hot abscess at the joint.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is that you put the ailing hand on a table and extend the arm, and the physician makes it equal, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and presses it until it returns.

des dois	It looks like the text has ended. This appears to be an Old French medical text, likely from the 14th century, and seems to describe a treatment for a dislocated ankle or foot. The text was written in a style that is reminiscent of medieval medical manuscripts, which often featured detailed illustrations and descriptions of surgical procedures.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two (parts) are healed, it is fitting to stretch them beautifully without effort, and that's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the lower back of the leg, then you must make the patient sit on one level or on a table entirely straight, and place your foot on this part of the joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it recovers.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is equal and nothing appears, then place under the heel of the foot a table on two legs, then strain firmly, and leave for three days, then loosen it; and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it has happened that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, since you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor too bold:
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and apply at the beginning soothing remedies, and let the patient be in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then cleanse the member now, so that the hot aposteme comes to pass.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is clean, then administer soothing remedies for the hot aposteme, and treat the wound as it should be with drying ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a break with the dislocation and small bones are splintered, then take them out, and do what we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this is worth more to you than your creator, and for the sake of your soul and body's salvation. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the Roman de Physique.
